For men, it happens within the lips that an abscess occurs hard as grains of wheat, either smaller or larger; then you must turn the lips and cut open each side, take with tweezers and strike in each part; then apply the leeve of vitriol powder over the incision until the wound is cauterized; and then soothe the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the chin
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a swelling arises on the chin called "albulus"; you must hold it with tweezers and strike at its root, allowing the pus or blood to flow; then apply vitriol powder or other drying powders over the wound, and if the swelling returns after the incision, which often happens, strike it again and cauterize it; it does not return again after cauterization; these are the shapes of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes sores are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scabs; and sometimes the teeth become black and yellowish and decay, as corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must make the patient sit in your hands, his head on your lap, and clean the teeth or scabs that are visible, until nothing remains; and in this way do with the blackness and greenness, and yellowing and other spots, as long as they are cleansed; and if one removes what is at the root first, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, as long as you have everything cleaned; and know that the teeth require different types of instruments to clean, according to the work that the barber demonstrates, because the razor with which one cleans between the teeth has other forms than that with which one cleans the root; and these forms and others should be provided for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure the tooth of its pain, it is necessary to delay drawing out as much as possible, for it should not be done at all; because this is a very high substance up until there is no excuse to shave.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Therefore, when the patient is forced to draw teeth, you must be certain about the pulling tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the patient suffers and believes it is a toothache, and draws the good tooth; but the pain does not go away as long as the evil remains, for we have seen this happen with saints; and when you are sure of the dying tooth, then it is necessary that you gouge around the tooth completely. Use a strong forceps to protect the gum from all sides; then move it to your hand or fine pliers at the first grip and grip, until it is well loosened; then tighten the pliers; and hold the patient's head in your lap so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After straightening the tooth correctly to break it, if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and gently push it in from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten, it is necessary that you fill it with bandages where the perforations are; and if you compress it gently with pliers, so as not to break while compressing; and it is very important to work skillfully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be careful not to break it, and leave a part behind, and the pain for the patient will return from the root even greater.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And be careful not to do as the ignorant lords often do, who in their haste and recklessness sometimes break a chariot, and do not bring about what we have described; but sometimes they cause this great disease due to the roots that remain or because the chariot is broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is removed, wash the area with wine or oil and lard; and if bleeding comes out, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which you mute the teeth first, should be long points and large handles, so that they do not bend as you draw the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be large enough that they do not bend when drawing the tooth and made of good iron, and be pointed to hold the tooth in place.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains drawn out, you must put soft cotton moistened with butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the limbs are smoothed, then insert the pliers called "algefri", by which the shoulder seems like a beak; and inside them make as if it were a file and this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these tongs, you must peel back the skin entirely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as a palindrome, in its place.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be thick and sturdy so as not to break, and if the root pops out with these tools, that is good; if it does not, help with all the instruments, as their forms are listed below.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses the instrument with two prongs, its form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments that are in front of the teeth, for this tool appears to be large pincers. Here is its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool should not break, and know that many tools are used for teeth; also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters discover by themselves their instrument according to what their craft and illness require, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the variety of cases, and if it breaks a chariot or another bone that it can, if it seeks the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, here is its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And should be large and firm to hold the bone, so it does not slip, but can hold and remove; then restore the joint with appropriate medicines, and if there is pus in the bone and it is small, grind everything with this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not appear according to natural form and are misshapen, especially in women who have not yet borne children, you should know that if the tooth is impacted after the dent (wisdom tooth) and is not properly aligned, it cannot be corrected: then remove it; and if it is near the dent, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, made of sharp iron at the end, and remove it.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle of the forceps should be used gently for many days due to the hardness of the tooth and because you do not move the others, and if it is possible, file it down with a small file in the shape as shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is the same as the file used to make needles; and file the tooth gently for many days, so that it does not move too much when it grows; then plane it flat at the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is excessively sharp and bites the tongue, you must file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth fall out.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth are loosened, either by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot press on it so that he eats without chattering, and you have cured them with constricting medicines, but this is of no use; then they must be held back with a gold thread, for silver threads become green and rot, but gold does not change; and the thread should be medium-sized neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth aligned, take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the shoulder between the separated teeth, if there is one or more, until you see clearly up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering until the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and skillfully, so that it does not move; and tie your knot at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then sew the head of the shoulder with thread using pincers, and assemble them and place it between the healthy teeth, making sure not to pierce the tongue; then keep it in this position as tight as it can remain without dislocating. If it dislocates or the stitches come undone, tighten with another thread; if it remains in place for a while and serves thus for its entire duration, this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you can see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, place it back in its socket, freshly and as we have said; and do not interfere if one is not skilled and patient, and sometimes a tooth-shaped bone of an animal is used, and placed in the place where it is missing, and tie it as we have said, and let it stay for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 There are times when a ligament comes under the tongue or is born in this way, or by accident due to a sutured wound; and the operation is such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head still, and pull the tongue aside. Then sew the nerve ligament wide enough for the tongue to be dislocated from its place, if there is hardness or knot, which is due to a wound being sutured; in this case, break it with an unguis and sew it wide open; make sure that the incision is not too deep, because there is an artery below it; when you have finished, raise the leg from cold water and ash, then put a linen tent under the tongue; tighten it each night so the leg cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if blood flow comes out, put vitriol powder on it; and if pus flows from it, cauterize it with the slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with another cure until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it of small color or black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards white and there is moisture, throw the onion, and cut it with a thin spatula from both sides; and if it turns black at your procedure, apply vitriol powder until it is burnt, then return to your procedure until you pull out all of it; then lift some lard oil and linen, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes a boil called "godath" comes into the throat, which are properly called two almonds. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the discharge of blood; but let it be until it becomes ripe, and then you will cut it open or it would burst by itself; and if it is of white color again, and the root is thin, prepare the instrument for covering, but first check if the abscess is cooled and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders should be in alignment, and open his mouth and take hold of him by the sergeant between his hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument as described; it is made of silver or fine iron like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue with the entire instrument and see the abscess, take a hook and pierce it into the almond, and pull it out above as much as possible; and pull any cloth away from it, then cover it with the instrument, as described here, which resembles something forceful; and although the head may be curved and one end to another, they are sharp, and made of iron or copper:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold it with pliers of this shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, use pliers with the following shape: and when you catch one of the nuts (peas), hold the other in the same way, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot, sharp, and warm water, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient again with hot water or cooked quince peels, or myrtle twigs, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then treat it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses than the two nuts may appear in the throat, if so catch them equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treat a woman of an abscess that was inside the throat, to be specific, an abscess of small size; and I had tightly closed the entire throat so that the woman could not exhale through the narrowed passage, nor eat or drink, and would have died if she lasted thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess had risen so much that it had burst through both openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I therefore immediately, and thrust into one of the openings, then pulled it out violently, and removed a large piece of bone; afterwards I reset it in the other wound near the neck, and opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; after that, I thrust the opening into these abscesses, and took a part of it, and no more blood came out; and thus the intestines were expelled from the throat of the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting off this abscess for a long time; and the abscess closed again and filled up the cavity that I had seen, until it became quite large; then I tied it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts, and let God do with them as He would after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the rectum protrudes towards the anus and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "anus".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 If the wound, as we have said in the division, is cured but does not improve, and you see that the abscesses are calmed and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is round and not long and red, black or blood-colored, then you should avoid incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it, as I have said according to its bladder and length, you must make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument we have mentioned before; then insert the cannula into the anus, draw it out, and cut it with the two instruments I mentioned in the incision of the two anuses.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cover anything beyond the natural term; for if you do, it causes harm to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use as we have said in the incision of the II amandres, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient fears to be covered, then you should use an instrument for the cauterization of the senses to alleviate fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the method of cautery is sharp fire.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient must place their head in your hand, and then press their tongue against the instrument as we have said or in the chapter of cautery, and hold it with a sharp-hot iron, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have some hair or oil where one applies the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument fully with all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on his side so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine without reaching the throat and the nose; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye for the amount of half an hour, until you see that the eye turns white and the redness caused by the medicine is alleviated; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with the cotton on top of the vein above, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; do this frequently until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for four or five days. If you have to start the cauterization again with the medicine, repeat it, and after the cauterization, irrigate around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, clean what is around the medicine; and moisten with cold water, and treat with gargarismes until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective by fumigation, not by cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camomile, yarrow, origanum, rue, and chamomile, and assemble them all or some of them in one pot, and put them inside, and make it boil; and let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and in the pot have one instrument comb-like according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the heads pushed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is putrefied; afterwards, it repeatedly occurs until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of an abscess's hot phase, for many things occur; and do not do this if for the declination of an abscess's hot phase.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 If this instrument is not present, take a canal and put an eggshell crack within the head of the patient so that his mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell crack does not allow the vapor to bother the mouth, and it is good treatment together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is necessary to insert a bone or fish spine into the throat, or some other thing; therefore, you must draw out what you can see, and press the tongue against the instrument until you see movement in the object; and whatever does not open and remains stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will expel the object through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of wool, or a radish root, or one morsel of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will adhere, and then you can draw it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of wood in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and lift the head high; be careful not to touch the epiglottis, as nothing should move or push the bone in; rather, the patient should push the instrument, because they must move or the thing is loose; if it is pushed down, or pulled back, move it evenly along the instrument until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the throat vein
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the medicine is bloodletting, as I mentioned in the division, through the use of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the patient's throat towards the sun, since you will press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the blood, draw it out very slowly with a small lancet, or fine tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that does not work, take a thick cane and push it into the patient's throat, then push or pull on the end of the cane with hot iron and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And let the patient be treated with water throughout the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, open the patient's mouth, pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with your hand frequently; and as soon as the blood is felt by the water, let it fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then the patient should be subfumigated with asafetida in the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, because it will persistently return.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The manner of fumigation is that you take the pot which has charcoal in it and cover it with a perforated cloth in the middle, and place the head of the instrument in it; then pour your fumigation on it, and have the patient put the head of the snake in his mouth and close his mouth so that no smoke escapes but comes directly to the anus; and the anus will soon become inflamed, and if it does not fall, then start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, eat salty and acrid things and drink nothing; and then it will be necessary for him to evacuate by this means.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the instrument used to treat the nostril is as follows, when it can be seen, resembling curved tweezers for entering the throat; and similar to a syringe tip, and it should have a sharp edge so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many things appear like abscesses, according to what is recalled afterwards in this book from one and another, and they are diverse in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways that one resembles the other, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for the cavities that are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses in the head are different from those in the cavities, and abscesses in hollow bones are different from those that come at joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscesses, one should not pierce them until the boil is ripe according to its completion; and if there are such as they must be pierced when they are hard, but do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that come at joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When an abscess comes near to a joint, and it is left until it bursts around it, in case the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 If the abscess is near the main member and you delay the perforation until it matures, it will harm the main member; or if it is near the base, piercing it before it has matured can cause the abscess to spread, resulting in an open wound, a fistula, and preventing healing within a long term. It is not advisable to pierce an abscess without digestion being completed, unless it is near the base, which cannot be perforated until it is full-grown, and straightened out within, and a fistula forms; and it cannot heal within a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the sign of the perforation of an abscess that is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, the disappearance of fever, the reduction of pain and redness, and the decrease in swelling and shrinking of the abscess's head, as well as other signs; and you should make the perforation sit lower or closer to the abscess, where it has started to move open; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places or areas without any pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that break, according to the same member. (direct translation)
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in the charnel (or putrid) place, it is beneficial to let the perforation remain until confirmation through complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it beforehand, the body will be flooded with its venom, and it will be filled with much filth; and by chance, the lips may harden and it may infect you deeply.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary to make small piercings for small abscesses, and large piercings for large abscesses, and numerous cuts according to the similarity of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where you need to cover them, they should be bandaged; when it has become as thin as cloth and is softened, it should be done as with babies: and if there are those that are cut into three angles, and those from which a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar cuts and bandages.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 He who has no head (like an abscess superficially), it is necessary that you pierce it fully; and when the abscess is large and has collected great pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing out incorrectly; do this many times gradually, until the pus is completely drawn out; similarly, if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old people debilitated.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 The pus may sometimes spasm with the discharge of it, which may happen that the patient dies, and you need not worry.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, proceed with great caution in this chapter, and when you have pierced the abscess, drain the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a large wound, bring threads of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess and there is much pus, it is necessary that you place a thread in each one so they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or with linen rags without moisture, tie it until the third day; then lance it, and cure with ointment until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and apply it to the cloth, wetting it repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and apply the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the limb or abscess is very nervous, you should put hot tents and damp cloths on it; if it is summer, and the limb is fleshy, you should put damp cloths on hot oil or cold water, or on oil and cold water for up to three days, as we have said; then remove the abscess and drain it and cure it until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This must be understood universally in the treatment of abscesses; now I have told you how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses coming from the head, there are ways that are in bandages, similar to the bag of a linen sack, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that have fat or moisture similar to pus; and there are some which are hard and stony in the cutting, and there is no doubt that the arteries do not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is that you explore with all instruments called "intermissor", from which the form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they make a long incision.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is drained, they scrape without leaving any hair that contains that moisture, because it returns immediately when left alone; then put cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise in oil and lime, and apply the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who have been delayed will recover.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then repeat the wool, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know that it does not stay in place; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess is fatty, squeeze it according to this form, longwise; and pour out your onions and the bark from all parts, and apply all your cure to draw out the coat where it lies; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And likewise treat the abscess if it is hard, and of cutting and caring for it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut above the hard abscess and moist it, it will be easier because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And for any of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and among those was the abscess I treated or head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had pierced it with anything, one would have made an equal wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or heads coming from children's heads and the roots of ears, they should be opened wide every day depending on the situation, in order to let pus out; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this abscess appears at the neck, beneath the chin, in armpits, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, they are swollen and connected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 Each scrofula is properly within its side, as the neck and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the resemblance of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 Some contain moisture, and there are some malicious ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the one that you see with good disposition to be touched, and resembles the color of the body, and is silent from all sides and is not arterial nor venous, and is not hollow; it must be cut open on top, and peel off each part, and place the two lips of the curette at the anuses, if you have need of them, as we have said in the abscesses of the head; pull gently and gently, and be sure to not cover the nerve or vein, and do not let the spatula or lancet touch, so that the hand does not tremble, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you open the vein or artery and it does not let you work on it, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that stop blood, and hold the wound closed; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound becomes soft and starts to pus.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood stops flowing, return to your work until you finish it; then check at your discretion if there remain small scrofulas, if so, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein near the root of the scrofulas, it is not necessary to cut the scrofulas at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang down without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 If you excise the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, for there will be no excess remaining due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you understand to cover the root and pull out the pus, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas that have excess, pierce there where it is swollen; and pierce it as the one mentioned above, in a dependent manner, then introduce poultices with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply an ointment to heal it until it is healed.
de squinance	The meaning seems to be about treating a scrofula (a chronic inflammatory condition), specifically when it becomes necrotic (rotten) and needs to be drained and sewn up. The term "de squinance" in the following sentence is not explicitly explained in this text, but it could potentially refer to the same condition or a related one based on the context. Here's the translation for this line:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke and described the measure of the throat, but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is their written words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, the slit in the throat called "epiglotte" should be opened; and aid should not be given by these, because all the veins and the passageways of the sickness are for those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the passageway, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should do so below three circles or four small slits through the middle, between the two circles or by the amount of the split at the symphysis, not in the cartilage; and the veins that supply it are long enough for this section of the epiglottis, provided that there is no cartilage.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 If the master is fearful, then it must be stretched out to the full length of the throat, then cut the cartilage until it reaches the trachea; and sever the blood vessels if you see anything, and then cut the symphysis as we have said; and this has been demonstrated by the section of the windpipe which protrudes through the broken larynx and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed where there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound with care, and sew it completely through the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce heat, until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged dead, and the wings are cut off.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then apply the throat (cautery) for this reason: because the patient cannot cough, and they breathe through the wound, in this way they are kept from death. And for this reason, the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the malignity of the disease has passed, which takes 3 or 4 days. Then they would command to sew up the wound and cure it; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 A young girl took the knife and thrust it into her throat, piercing parts of the windpipe; I was summoned to cure her but found her lifeless.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and saw that blood was coming out of it, and I knew that it had neither opened nor conducted air except through the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastily sewed up the wound and cured her until she was healed, and it never happened to the girl that her voice became hoarse, and she returned to her health; for this reason I say that in such a case of the windpipe there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	in the throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and is a large abscess in color like a goiter, and is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; where natural has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 The accidental type is also of two kinds: one is similar to fatty tissues, and the other kind is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; there should be fear, and it should not be operated on unless in the case of a small one, and prove and search thoroughly at every entrance; if you find it as fatty tissues and does not spread, when you cut it, take out all its covering, if there is any; and carefully encircle it, and cure it until it becomes perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of ours exist, which I will describe all their similarities; now it is necessary for me to say the entire difference between notch and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Dislocation is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the swelling has passed and the fracture has healed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 The notch has no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains the pus, which is its own sac and is of the same color as the body, and begins like an abscess, and becomes large; and they have two similarities: either fatty or moist, and many colors are like what I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the newt, that you test and examine first everything in the instrument called "entromissoire", according to what its shape comes or the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 The method for the incision of abscesses is that you take a place more moist than what you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little until you feel the abscess has been pierced, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the pus, and be careful so it does not spout.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs from the ulcer, make it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after opening, moisture does not come out, know that it is filled with fat; then make a cross-shaped incision, grab it with forceps, peel it gently on each side and pull the skin or coat that you can pull safely along with it; and if you cannot pull it safely, pull it apart in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If there remains anything, it comes back many times; and if a small amount remains and does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powder to the wound, hold it closed with bandages, place warm soothing things on the abscess, and heal it with other treatments until it is healthy; and if it is large, cut the edges of the wound in two, and heal the one that emits pus.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or otherwise is contrary to you, and you hurry and apply vitriol powder, let it lie for two or three days, until the wound heals, and allow the boil of blood to subside; then return to cover what remains unhealed with a new dressing.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Here are the forms of the probing instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three crosses which are called 'albaret', and one that is called 'breb', and there are also three kinds for encircling abscesses: large, medium, and small, to probe the fistulas; and they are similar to needles used for sewing, and they are made of citron wood, or iron, or silver, and yellow ones are more valuable, and they are more skilled at penetrating black plungers for encircling the swellings of the fistula; and they are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the wound.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the tumors are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and some tumors have two humps in three ways; and some tumors have three humps, and they are also of three types; and some tumors have two humps, and tumors with a single hump, and they are also of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The tips of these are sharp, and those who do not cut only from one side, so as to avoid striking the vein or nerve; and these instruments used for insertion are called almelles and they are placed in several positions, so that the patient does not feel pain at the opening of abscesses; and there are three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and it is not used elsewhere except for charnut (charred) areas such as legs, arms, breasts, and ulcers, and sometimes another similar instrument is made smaller, resembling fistula stitches, according to this shape, to stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at the site that heals quickly, at the veins, and sometimes returns according to this large form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, until they seem like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and those who wish to cure them should do so according to this form of the line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then remove the fat and apply medicine to the wound, then bring together the two lips of the wound at stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast tilts downward due to its size, as happens with women, then split it into two halves above, by two similar cuts; thus one should hold the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form from line b to g; then remove the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and introduce what has been said for stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not wish to rest, or due to the discharge of blood, then fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it digests the remaining fat, then heal it when it is drained.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses of the saddle (a type of boil)
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the saddle are types of hard scrofulas with ridges, and if they contain moisture within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those containing moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b up to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole boil which is in the abscess is emptied, place old cotton on the wound, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and apply an ointment to it until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, make incisions in it as we have said for scrofula, and if pus forms in the wound, apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the cutting of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is punctured and the skin is closed above it, there are often abscesses; and the same happens with the vein that has burst and formed an abscess; and when you recognize it by the artery, the abscess extends deeply; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels tight; and when it is caused by the vein, it swells noticeably away from the surface; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the shoulders and angles and near the neck and in many other places, and it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is required to cauter the iron cure, and the one who is at the head should also be cauterized; in the one who is swollen with an artery, make an incision through the skin lengthwise; then open the abdomen carefully, cut the artery from the tendons, until it is exposed; then insert a needle, and pierce it up to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then push the thumb between the two bands until the swelling subsides and is drained; then bind the wound with a bandage until it heals; if the swelling is due to the opening of a vein, then you should stain your hand with it as much as you can from the wound, then insert a needle under the place you hold in your hand, pierce it and have it carry a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other side; then tie the wound, as I told you, or bind it with one of the two bands with a thread; if you doubt that the threads will stick, then insert another needle through all the thread under the wound at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cut the swelling until it subsides, then cut the superfluous fat and leave what is tied; then put a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply treatments with tent and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	From abscesses of the flesh
