Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As in arteries and veins, abscesses come to the nerves when they are struck or due to excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this often happens at the shoulders and fingers in all places where there are joints, and it is called abscesses, and its color resembles the body's color, and it is found in various positions with pain; and when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not completely within the body, but under the skin; and it should be treated carefully from all sides, and it does not go forward or backward, neither up nor down, and the one who is in joints must not be covered with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and those who are on the head or forehead, rub with spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, take tweezers and press it at its root; if it is large, open it with an incision, peel off the skin, then bone and close the wound with stitches, and let it heal until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Heavy growths hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "funge" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large heads; some are small and some are very large; I have seen a man who had two bellies that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had narrow roots, and were cut open, and moisture flowed out of them immediately.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I cut and found one weighing 18 ounces in the other 6, and the work in the incision is such that if you look at it, the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist with a narrow root; if you cut with a large spatula, be present the cautery fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in the thigh, there often come too great displacements of blood, and if it persists, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient fearful and afraid of the iron incision, take a thread made well, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then pull it tight, and do not stop pulling the thread of pledget until it stops the flow, causing pain; and if the roots are thick, be careful to cauterize the same place again, lest it recur; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cauterize the one who is of dark color, poor sensation, and milky eyes.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess swollen, and I will come to the treatment for gonorrhea afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil bursts out
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of boil comes from a cautery of wound or split in the scrotum (as it happens in other routes), and it is above the abdomen and among some of the testicles, as it happens elsewhere, or due to blood flowing from veins or arteries, as described earlier, or due to swelling; and if it comes through the route of the scrotum and the exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and has an open wound with multiple exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the intestine, then it is more diverse. When you press it with your fingers, it retracts and then comes back, and in some cases, it becomes hard, and greatly swells at the entrance of the wound, and due to much labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and easily pressable without constraint; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and are filled according to a certain amount; and if it is due to swelling, it is soft to touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to the blood of an artery, or vein, or swelling.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 It is necessary that you let the treatment continue.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For it has doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 If the appearance is due to the intestine or the belly, you must instruct the patient to bend his back and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the swelling; then command him to lie down between your hands; then go around the side that you have signed with a spatula; then cut half of the abscess above with a large spoon; then tie it around with a strong thread or a strong cord firmly, and tighten the ligature; then open the half of the abscess stretched out over the ligament, and insert your finger; if you find it caught in the ligament, release it, and push the intestine out of the belly; and if you find the swelling, take it with the spoon and drain the excess; and if the arteries or veins oppose you, go around, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two thick threads, and insert the needles around what you have made in a cross that you pierce; then press the abscess over the needles for four leagues, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the side as it is, and let the dead flesh rot by itself; or cut when it becomes tender and can be pierced, then cure what is necessary, and close the abscess as we have said; drain the pus or moisture that you find, then cure the side of what is needed, and sew the side.
dou chancre	of the abscess
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of abscess, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how one should administer fire-cautery; and we will say the abscess is in joints, and great caution must be taken in its treatment, and the ancients said that when abscesses are on a place where they can be shaved like an abscess which is on the face, or on the thigh, and in similar places, and it should all be removed when it is at the beginning; but when it is large and old, it does not have to be approached, for I never knew anyone to heal it, nor has anyone healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when they are in place and can be removed as we have said, it is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him urinate if he has manifest repletion, then prepare the patient. That is, shave the area to be operated on cleanly; then dip your fingers or a lancet in boiling water and cauterize the vein or artery you are going to operate on; then wait for all the blood to come out, and press the area well with your hand or something, and if the flow of blood opposes the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then heal him by other means until he is healed.
de ydropisie	And from the dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs for each similarity, and the cure done with medicines, and that which is cured with iron: it is only eclipsed; one should not touch iron in these two similarities: namely tympanites and ypsarche, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when you treat this similarity of dropsy called "eclipsed" with medicines, if the cure does not help, observe whether the patient is weak or if he has another disease other than dropsy, such as swollen belly and similar things; do not touch iron in that case, for there is doubt. And if you see the patient of strong constitution, and he has no other disease except dropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed as follows: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the assistant presses the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the buttocks, then take the pointed spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut through in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be pierced without entering so much that it does not reach the intestine when thrust in, and cannot be bent; then check if the yolk sac is attached towards the intestines: if so, you must cut below the navel III fingers directly above the handle; and if the yolk sac is due to liver disease, it should be on the left side of the navel III fingers; and if it is due to mucus, it should be on the right, and the patient should not lie on the incision lest the superfluidities run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push, and place your hand at the entire spatula between the skin and the sac as when peeling an apple of the quantity of a nail or so; then pierce the sac until the spatula reaches the water level, and this is the bladder, then draw it out, and push this instrument from where it is shown here:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a thin silver needle, and is of linen or light thread, and in the lower part, there are three holes; on one side, two holes; and one on the other; and the head of the shoulder is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes carve a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 In the upper part is the anus, so when the instrument comes to the water, push it now on the instrument; then empty either half or one third part, for if you empty more than necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he falls down, or approaches death; but empty according to its power, and according to what the dispositions of the power of the patient and his pulse indicate; then move the instrument and stop the water, and it is now held in check by the plug that seals the wound where you have pierced, as I spoke, that you pierce in this manner; then begin moving the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering from water, and draw a small amount of water; do this every day, and take care not to let it linger but only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt about the patient and let him have much water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and anoint him with wine; and cure him with drying medicines until he is dry, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the vein
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born who do not have foreskins at the penis, or the foreskin is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary to pierce through all the spittle very thinly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then put the thin foreskin of wood on it, tie and hold it for three or four days or until it wants to urinate, if it is removed then, and let him urinate, and then replace it; and sometimes it may not be necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 For the person whose ulcer is small, it is treated with a poultice of cloth, as we have said, and it will open up.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the ulcer in its place are bled, because no one is born with an ulcer at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating before they raise their penis; and they cannot enjoy intercourse due to this, because the matter cannot reach the opening, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the work is that the patient lies supine on their back, with the head of the penis and the tip likewise like the size of a feather, so that the testicles hang in the scrotum, as required; and take care to avoid leakage of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, stop the bleeding from the wound, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the genital sores
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this ulcer appears on the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly genitals; and in it there are malignant and non-malignant ones; you should take them once a week with a subtly thin tool, and cut and clean all of them, then put damp cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with diaphinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, with pus-like color and swelling, then you should apply a fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cut it and if the ulcer is below the penis, having part inside the skin and part outside, you must remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it has healed, you should take care of the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you treat it (the shoulder), do not be sure that the joints of the rod will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come into the rod and the surrounding area; if so, everything that is black and corrupt must be cut away, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour, which should be made from the bark of pommegranate seeds and other similar things, then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if there is discharge of blood, bring the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cauteries assist the two conditions together: namely, in the discharge of blood and corruption; and if the joints of the rod are corrupt and recede, you must bring or guide from the rod a plunging cane made of yew wood, and make the patient urinate; and when the hairs have risen to the head of the rod that is in those who have not been circumcised, or there is pain or abscess, it is necessary then to shave it with a razor, until the ligaments are loosened, and the joints of the rod are released from all sides; and if this is a painful thing to say to them, you must shave it at the spatula, any little bit from the head of the rod and the skin; then separate them well, and put a thin linen cloth dampened with cold vinegar between them so that they do not adhere again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in terms of healing; however, when we perform this work on our own accord and specifically for children, it is necessary that we do the best job possible and make it as light a wound as possible to heal quickly.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients would not circumcise their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the greater part of masters and nobles who performed circumcision around age one day, and for all newborns; however, it was feared because there were two layers, and by chance if the upper one was cut, the lower one remained.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now cover it with copper, and the pain is doubled; at the amputation which is close to the limb's point, the cutting edge of the iron may slip off, and ruin the work, and many times it grows in such a way that there is no need for amputation and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	I have found the advantage of using ligatures in amputations, because the force cuts equally well above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, you should cut it evenly all along; but make sure the thread is tightly wrapped around the skin; and the method for the first operation should be such that you make the child understand, if it can, that you tie the thread only around the rod, and then let it rest in every possible way you can; then let it remain between your hands straight, and restore its strength between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then push your hand onto the rod and blow or cut, and pull it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it well of the filth that has accumulated there, then tie a double thread around the opening, then tie it over the one thread to the knuckle and the index finger, and bind between the two threads, then untie the thread quickly and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood flow freely and flow, for this is the purge; and sprinkle powder on it and sprinkle rose oil cooked egg white mixed with fresh rose oil and wrap the egg white around it until the next day, and treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for cleaning is as follows: the two heads should be soft and pointed, and they should be as large as a finger equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the cores within are at incision; therefore, you must extend it to your nail, so that the lews become abscesses; and strike it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, grasp it with pliers, and then strike.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If they pass more than three days and that which is below the worm is swollen, let it be until the abscesses subside, and gently scrape it; if you can move it, strike it as you can, and keep away from the part of the worm, this will do no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the limb with submerged wounds using the powder we have said or treating powders, and if you strike too harshly, it will go up, but this will not harm; treat it as we have said until it heals.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to a stone, frozen blood, pus, frozen semen, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not relieved, and you see it is retained by a stone lodged in or at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over his knees; his feet should be placed on the back, and he should extend his abdomen from the upper part above the lower back, and hold the patient as tightly as possible; then the neck of the bladder should be compressed to express the stone above it, so that the urine is released; if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe", of which this is the form: and it should be made of fine subtle silver tubing, like the feathers of a bird; and the tube should be one palm and a half long, and should be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the method of the issue of the urine is as follows: You take a double thread, tie one end to the head of a linen or cotton rag, and insert the other end into a syringe; and tie off the excess of the linen and insert it into the top of the syringe, then oil or butter the syringe and dip the penis and scrotum in oil moistened with olive oil and warm water; then gently introduce the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base of the penis; then bend the penis over towards the anus; then insert the syringe up to the bladder, and make the patient feel that urine is coming out into the empty container, and this is not done according to this order unless because the conduit through which it flows is twisted; then pull the thread completely through the linen, and urine will follow the linen, then extract it forcefully, and correct the urine; and continue the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorchures or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is collected there, and you see it distill liquids and medicines, do everything with the instrument called "clepsydre," and its form is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed and if it has three openings: two from one side, and one from another, as you see; and the medicines should be such that they stop the worm without adding anything, if one can draw out the moisture, and push as necessary; and when you see your medicines expelled into the bladder, place the head of the syringe in the moisture, and draw with the drawing motion that is there; if you draw out the moisture with the syringe, then forcefully push back the drawing motion within; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; this is the form of the subtle enema with which one cleanses the bladder: this is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or lead, and the head is higher; below it lies the chest or ribs; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the masticator that you use to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between two breasts using strong thread; heat the masticator over the fire; then insert the head of the clistere into the wound, hold your hand on the bladder all around the masticator until the patient feels that the masticator has reached the wound; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, puncture it roundly; then push the strong thread into these holes, assemble the circle like a shield, put inside it oil and masticator and water, seal it in the instrument; and do the same with the wound, pressing your hand until the masticator reaches the wound.
de la piere	from cutting into stones
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone and extraction with medicines; and I have told the difference between a set stone in the rain, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work with cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder, resembling water in its subtleness; it opens wounds, injures the patient's penis, pierces many times, then binds it; and at most these leaps cause foundation problems. And children recover easily until they are four years old, but it is very serious in adults, and it is mild to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes blocks the stone (arrow or bullet).
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take hold of the patient by the feet and push and move them downwards, so that the stone descends into the bladder, and at times moves upwards; then have the patient sit with his hands hanging down between his legs, so that the bladder is completely declined towards the lower part; then grasp it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry to cut on top of the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall at your touch, moisten your finger of the left hand if the patient is a child, or use oil if the patient is an adult, and press it onto its base, and grasp the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press towards your finger, and push it out through the place where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch his right hand upward and remove the skin that is under the scrotum in the part where the cutting is done; then insert the spatula covering it, which is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And they make an incision between the coccyx and the base of the sacrum, not in the middle but along the left side of the coccyx; and it should be straight across the stone, and your hand should be either against the base or the coccyx, and the incision should be wide on the outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, the pressure on the hand that is against the base may cause it to jump out due to the effort; and know that there is a certain stone where there are angles and margins: it is necessary to extract it; and if there is one that is rounded, similar to a plum pit, and round, from which the issue is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Therefore, where there are angles and margins, make the incision larger; if it does not come out, you must pull up on pliers that are shaped like a chisel at the tip, to force the stone out so it does not escape; or push the instrument with a subtle curved tip into it; and if you cannot trick it in this way, widen the hole slightly, and if it is not rounded, squeeze it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first pull out the largest one from the opening of the bladder, then pound on it, pull it out, and then the smaller ones if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it must be made larger by making a bigger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 There are two things that happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes out quickly because the wound cannot heal; but still you must try to drain it, or break the nails with pliers as much as possible while draining it; and when you have completed your work, you should fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and hold it closed, and put on top a damp linen cloth in oil and vinegar, or in oil and cold rose water and cold water, to soothe the abscess heat; then lay the patient on his neck, and do not undo the bandage until three days have passed.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen [the bandage], moisten the wound well with oil and water, then apply the ointment defyndicon and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if an abscess comes in the wound and the corrosion, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and the urine is retained due to this in such a way that without jumping with urine: then press your thumb into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause diarrhea; then lift the wound from pus and ease and oil, and help it in all ways you know, until it heals; and it is necessary that every hour that you care for it, you bind the two thighs, and place the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the wound is small, and it is conducted by the penis and pierced through, and urine cannot flow out; you should cure it in this way: cut it many times, or be excused from cutting due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron fork according to this shape and sharpened at four angles on one thong:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the thread and tie it around the penis under the stone, so that it does not return to the bladder; then push the awl lightly into the penis, until it reaches the stone; and turn the awl little by little in the stone, as much as you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what is left of the stone inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken and jumps out with the urine, the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread around the stone below and another above, then direct the penis towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the woman's stone (meaning: uterine stones or ovarian cysts)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it ever occurs, the treatment is grave, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that by chance the woman may be a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well how to examine herself, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third method is that by chance one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that the stone of a woman is deeper than that of a man, because it requires a more profound incision and great fear ensues. If such a case arises, then you must seek out a midwife who knows, and if she can't be found, then take a subtle one; and present to her a wise bailiff in the affairs of women or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her that she does what you command regarding the investigation of the stone; and ensure that the woman is a virgin: Then you must press your finger or base into it and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then she should constrain it under her finger, and I command her to press her finger or hand on the patient, and urge her left hand upon the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is found [the dislocated shoulder], then you must gradually move it from the entrance of the bladder until under the hip bone, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike on the bone in the root of the thigh near the middle of the femur, where it is moved apart, and feel the bone in that area; do not move your hand above or below the bone, and keep it small [in size]; then press the thumb into the hip, if you feel the bone so close the wound as much as the bone can protrude, and know that there are many types of bones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 Recognize the symptoms to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if it (the wound) opens again, put vitriol powder on the spot and hold for an hour until it stops bleeding; then return to your work, as long as the stone is still there, and have tools that I told you about in the extraction of the stone from men to help you in your work; and if it opens again and it is the artery that was cut, put powder on the spot and bind it with straps and bandages, do not continue this, and leave the stone and do not draw it out, for the patient may die accidentally; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood is relieved and the wounds have healed, return to your work until the stone is expelled.
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	In other words, aquose is not something else but an assembly of moisture or white pus that is under the sac of the kidneys, which contains the egg; and it is called "white pus", and sometimes it is properly within the egg's membrane itself, if one believes it to be another egg; and it is the skin of the kidney between the white pus we have mentioned, and it does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this aquose is due to weakness that comes from the kidneys, and this matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there comes percussion on the eyes, and this moisture has many colors: either it declines to yellow, or without redness, black or whitish, and this happens more often; these are signs for recognizing this gathering, because if it is white as we have said, it is a good abscess, long like an egg, and do not open the eyes, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the cloth itself, abscesses become reasonable with part of the egg, and for this reason it is believed to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the hide of the skin and the white flesh, it can be felt well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, probe thoroughly to find out its form, which is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this which follows the intrusion, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When we treat it with iron (meaning cauterize), the patient should be anesthetized according to our ability and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back on something slightly elevated, and cover him with many cloths; then lie him on his left side, and command the attendant to stand on the right, and stretch out the arm at one of the two armpits near the hide of the skin; then take the spatula, and cut the hide of the skin along its length up to the end of the finger, and make your incision straight in cutting the hide of the skin down to white flesh, and peel it off carefully according to your ability; then pierce the white flesh fully with water until it is hollowed out, and drain all the water, and then place your thumbnails, and push the white flesh up; and do not touch the hide of the skin, but only the white flesh; cut all around it carefully, making sure you cut it well, for if you do not, the water will return; and if the egg breaks during your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the white flesh; then bring together the two sides of the hide near the armpit into a stitch, then treat it like other wounds until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupt with other disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, suspecting the flow of blood; then strike the cone at the entire suspended area, and extract the egg, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an ulcer is assembled in two parts together, know that these are the branches; if you strike the other part as you did the first equally, then draw out the blood, and put damp linen in oil of roses into the wound; and put another damp linen in wine and oil on it, and put over the two cysts, and put over them doubled cloths, and tie it all with a string according to this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths, and use them with damp linen in this shape and sewn together into a collar for the thigh, and one of the heads takes hold under the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the handle; and the other head on the two angles, and assemble all the rest in the knot of the garter; and sometimes this branch of cautery is used instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take the cautery cutter thinly, and strike the leather of the cysts, and heat them as we have said, so that the white pus from the ulcer is exposed; then take the cautery in this shape, and pierce that pus with a small hole, and peel off that thin cauter with hot iron:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cup in all ways that you can, while you are heating it; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg (meaning "yolk"); and know that this work is more wholesome; and pay attention to the lack of bleeding, and perform the operations of cutting; and if anything prevents you from doing so, or an abscess bursts or a flow of blood or something else occurs, then treat what prevents you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 If the patient is afraid and does not want to endure this operation due to its horrible appearance, then perform perforation as I told you before, and know that when you are certain, by the signs we have described, that the abscess has been opened, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; next, pierce the abscess in the area below the whole spatula-like blade, and place the perforation along the length of the body; ensure that the wounds are wide so that all the pus can flow out; then put cotton over the area and hold it in place, allowing the remaining pus to drain, and treat until the wound is healed; if the white cloth does not let the pus come out through the opening of the wound, you must insert a reed or instrument for letting out pus from dropsy, as described before; enlarge the opening of the wound, know that the pus will return, and it will be collected after six months or so, and when it is collected as described before, the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the knees
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the treatment of this disease, there are many precautions because of its multiple forms, therefore it seems more suitable to leave it [the disease] untreated; and I will tell you the treatment and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from the body, and especially the eyes; this happens in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is by excessive sour and feverish spreading in the joints, or by impact; and the abscess's color depends on the body's color; and there is no pain, and the abscess is serious; and sometimes an abscess is hard and stony, of that color, and on occasion it comes from an artery, or from a vein inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 If it comes from an artery, this is known by the hot abscess position when you press it with your fingers; and it is not advisable that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 A person with swelling of the vein is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch on the fingers, and he can well make an incision on this resemblance, and on others; and it is that you cut the core of the bones, then is the yolk in the upper part, and the white thread stretches out, and delivers the suspensory from all parts of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the yolk is already swollen with these resemblances born, then you must draw out the yolk and cut it; if it is at the white thread or in that which is within the vessels, you must deliver all of that tender part and cut roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the birth of the placenta is on the back side, then you must crush the whole thing and draw out the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, apply the wound with dampened wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then heal it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the knees
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping resembling a thorn, with the softening of bones, and the patient becomes silent with great pain when he goes; and the cure for this disease is indeed as fearsome as what has been mentioned above, and nevertheless we will tell you its work, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 You must make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then push the suspensioner of the testicles downwards towards your hands, to all the things nearby the penis, and tie them with strings, and stretch them out; then cut a deep slit in the scrotum from one side to the other, so that they are exposed, and then peel it apart from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples; then insert a double-threaded needle there, and tie it at the first place where the blood vessel appears, and tie it again at the other end; then hit it accurately, directly along the length of the body, removing the corrupted matter; then treat the wound as one would treat an arrow wound, so that no testicle falls out due to the incision of the scrotum; for this is not harmful, and if all the testicles are present, you must draw the testicles back at each opening; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the scrotum, and they dry up and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	From the cutting of the siphac
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The manifestations of this hernia occur through a section that comes out or is extended on the abdomen in the area of the groins; due to this, the intestines descend from that rupture towards one of the kidneys. This rupture can be either of the syphac or of its extension and there are two ways of it happening: through percussion, jump, fall, lifting of heavy objects, and similar things. The signs that it is a hernia of the syphac are that it occurs little by little over a long time and does not happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the fullness, because the hernia follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the symptoms are when it is of the section where the intestines are cut open, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear variously beneath the skin near, and this is due to the exit of the intestines and the body expelling them through the opening of the incision.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines burst out from the anus and are retained within, causing great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is fear, for which it is necessary to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	1. And the method of work is that you command the patient to pull the intestine with their hand inside through the wound, if it can enter; then hold its neck on top of its body between your hands, and separate the legs; then raise the skin above, and cut all the fat from the flanks completely; then insert fingers of one hand into the openings required to open the wound, and make them such that the intestines can come out; then scrape off the attached fat that is under the skin of the flank, until the white fat is completely exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger into the place where the intestine was, in the place between the white fat under the skin of the abdomen, and the second layer of fat, and separate what is behind the abdomen, and the second layer of fat; then turn the intestines with your right hand inside the fat of the flank, and expose the white fat to your left hand, and lift the abdomen towards the back; and command the assistant to stretch the abdomen upwards, and separate what is in front of the ligament; and feel with your fingers if the intestine is twisted or hard white fat, and if you find anything, push it into the abdomen; then take a needle with thick thread made from ten threads, and insert it in the rear part of the fat, after the skin of the flank; after the abdomen, then cut the pieces that appear to have threads, until there are four threads; then arrange them one on top of the other like a cross, and tie the fat, which is under the skin of the flanks, with a strong cord of two fingers wide; then wrap the threaded pieces and tie them again with a cord of two fingers, so that no vassals who nurse it can enter inside, except for clean cloth; and place the cord immediately in the same place as the first cord, and after these two cords leave the fat which is under the skin of the flanks a long distance of one finger; and after all the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the flank, as far as it needs to correct, and bend it, as we have said earlier; then apply oiled linen cloth to the wounds, and apply the cord that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white ones are cauterized as we have said, after incision, due to fear of bleeding out.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this happens frequently, and let the ligament remain until it has chosen to loosen itself; and if it is slow in falling out, it should be softened with hot water, and place on it what was previously mentioned, until it has loosened completely; then cure the wound with another treatment until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dares to heal by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like a graft that is attached to the bone, in this manner that you tie the vessels after the cutting of them gently below; then break it in half, and treat the abscess with what was mentioned, until the vessels have loosened; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
