Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes rottenness comes in the entrails, as previously mentioned, and no intestines should be drawn from the anus; and if some do come out, it is bad, and repair it every hour; and yet if it remains too long in that place, the wound or syphilis occurs, because the intestines are extended, as previously mentioned, for it is stretched out, then softened and inflamed the entrails and opened; and the healing is done by cautery, as previously stated; and sometimes it is healed by iron in this manner: and the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then break the swollen part of the rottenness with a width according to the size of three fingers; and then pull out the syphilis that is below the skin, then take the rod and place it on the visible part of the syphilis; and press towards the abdomen, then cut the two visible parts of the syphilis onto the head of the rod, and cut one and the other; then pull out the head of the rod, but do not cover or extend the egg nor any other thing, as I have told you in the treatment of the intestinal graft; then heal by wound treatment.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads (of a wound), if they burn and heal the wound, let it remain open until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The blister is constricted, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved to this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the knees
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the knees becomes soft in some men, because the charms inside are made soft and there is pus visible; and it is necessary, when it is seen to be cured, that you make the patient lie on his back, and bind the softened skin over the natural skin; then gather the two lips together into a stitch, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin in four or six stitches firmly; then bind between the stitches, and let the cure be as for other wounds, until it is healed, and bind the thread.
dou chastrement	The correction or punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 I will omit the charms that are enlisted in our law, as it would be inappropriate to discuss them in this book; and there is no need to speak of them except for two reasons: one is that the mirrors in a charm respond when asked, and offer a cure; and the other, because we often have need of charms on certain animals to help us, such as bulls and sheep and cats and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say therefore that charms are made in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the one that we do by attraction, sit the animal in hot water until its limbs are softened and remain in this state; then take hold of it with your hand, and keep it in place until you no longer feel it.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 From the castration of the animal: you must first dye the beast, and press its scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspension cord, and strike each testicle with the hammer where you have well scored; leave no small amount of skin or fine skin which is on the vessels; and this method of castration is better than the one made by attraction, because at attraction something remains accidentally in the scrotum, causing the beast to desire lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism is according to the two ways in men: one where there is an opening between the two scrotums as the figure of woman's nature has, with hair, and sometimes in court the urine flows.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And another way it is with women, and it has above the penis like a rod and they copulate.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for men and women is to copulate all the affected areas, and treat them like other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the penis, it has no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tension
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 An ulcer that is adjacent to the natural part and is too ugly to see is called a tentigene, and some women have one as large as a hand, and this is the treatment for it.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 It is necessary that you stain the excess of the tentigene with your hand or onions and lightly copulate it; do not go too deep, so that no excessive blood comes out, then cure it until it heals; and at another ulcer that grows from the mouth of the husband, and it bursts and forcibly discharges pus, and is similar in appearance to a cow's udder, and because of this it was called by the ancients "the disease of cows".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said in the prescription, and cure it until it heals.
de erratique	Of the dislocated joints
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 It is erratic when the nature of a woman is not perceptible or small; it can be natural at birth, or accidental due to disease that comes about in this way; or it can be through unnatural union, or by subtle or gross artifice, and it is made full in marriage, or in ribs, or sideways, or however it may be; and they must try to conceive and give birth, and unfortunately the flowers may not come to fruition; and this knowledge is obtained through observation of the woman's belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the obstruction is close to appearing, either at your hand or at your side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is a subtle pain nearby the liver, and it is close to the breasts, hurry and do the following: place your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back with legs spread open; then form the two breasts round so that the subtle pain is firm, and cover them with oil-soaked wool; then lie the woman down every day so that she cannot touch herself.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 If it is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula resembling the leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the discharge is made of new flesh, stop it with onions and cut it; and have the medicines made from blood-stoppers, like acacia, dragon's blood, incense, combined abundantly with egg; then prepare a wide tube of linen cloth so that the wound cannot heal; and in this way, let it be long, and provide a dry tent of flax; then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when in marriage snow comes, it should be covered in this manner, unless abscesses are aggravated.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For to the aggravated abscess in marriage, one should not touch to do it.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which, without court, are not treated as usual, and when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into throbs; and we have said in the division their similarities, and signs, and I will say here those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and throbs, when they are full in marriage, and do not appear to touch, should not be cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those who are at the mouth of the vagina, they can be felt, are those which one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you should place the woman in a cold house, then stretch her legs at the ankles, break the leg at its roots, then sprinkle medicinal powders that restrict blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood powder and incense, and similar things; then leave her feet exposed for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and ivy leaves, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if bleeding stops, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If this does not stop bleeding, make it bleed again at the back and breasts without wounding; then take linen, wet it in plantain juice or elder juice with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess subsides, treat the place with ointment until it heals; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough crust, if necessary cover it as I have said in the thelul; and then continue treating it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	the abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many kinds of abscess come in marriage (a metaphor for the body), such as carbuncles, painful abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Therefore, I will tell in this treatise the treatment of hot abscess that comes in marriage (the body), which is not one of those that stick to the skin; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is acute at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hurry to pierce, but let it heal as long as the pain is alleviated; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats or one where he can lean, and support him on his back and gather his legs at the parts away from the leg; and let his thighs be spread out, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligament; then bring the ball towards the right side, and bring the instrument used to open the mouth of the bladder, from which the shape follows; and it is necessary that when you bring this instrument, that you pierce the tip first to know the depth of the bladder, so that what enters within of the instrument does not go too deep as it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the bladder with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary that you place the horn of the instrument above, and mark the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess is opened, and one touches it with a soft hand, it should be covered with a spatula of lard; and when the boil is emptied, you must put damp linen cloths in oil of roses or green dry oil into the wound; and place the damp cloth from the wound to the full extent of the marrow, and place over the marrow and over the tendon a clean, damp linen cloth soaked in vinegar or malvaceae that have been cooked; then heal it after two days of ointment following this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the marrow and the wound with a clyster of vinegar and honey, and then with vinegar or longis aristolochia that have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is healed in a marriage (scar tissue), you must be careful not to burn it with iron, but rather treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is necessary at the beginning for the woman to recognize the shape of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see her dilate afterwards and desire to urinate; then hasten the birth of the child; then know that this childbirth is according to nature's figure, and it issues from the head, and the second one comes with it; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly so that the child is born quickly; for when it descends on its head, the second one also comes with it, and the membranes of the birth are cleansed from excess by good cleansing; and he who comes in another way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 It sometimes happens that something falls upon the feet, or the body or shoulder, or the hands, or upon the belly, or back, and it may turn around the neck, or in other bad ways; therefore it is necessary for a wise and skilled baler to be there, and to avoid error and deception. I will show you all the figures as to how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out upon its head by natural childbirth, and the woman labors painfully, and her strength is weak, let her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert the small spatula between her legs in the form shown:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 Then cut the second finger, and strike its nail where the moisture that is inside is located; and hold the woman's belly until the baby comes out, and if it does not come out, you must fumigate her with musk from fenugreek with camomile oil; then make her take and vomit some concoction, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: thus the baby will now come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out, you must gently pull them back bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on the seat, and lift her feet up; then turn the seat on the ground, and hold the woman so she does not move when turning it; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, strike the hands with the knife that is placed before, extract the child, and pull back equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the birth of the child upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes upon its feet, you must push it upwards; and then turn it bit by bit until it is equal; then take hold of its feet and stretch them out bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 If it can jump up to any height, when commanded to seize and make it vomit from fear, and if it jumps away, then may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it bit by bit until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it will be easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if it does not come away as we have experienced, then say to take musk, from high places, and oil of ambergris, and melted resin, and grind all in a mortar; and put the nature of a woman within it and apply this ointment on the outside; then make her sit in hot water until below the ribs; and when she is softened below, apply collyrium of myrrh and place it on her, and leave her for an hour; then have her sit on a seat, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, because the infant now jumps around.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's excrement over its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, place it on its back with its hands folded one over the other; then lay it on its neck, let the feet hang downwards, and lie it on the bed; bend the hands little by little, then take hold of them above the belly, and remove the hips from below until it is arranged properly below; if the child does not come out, seize the feet and push them strongly, then push the belly upwards, then put your hands; pull the child little by little; and command the woman to hold herself as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the delivery of the child that comes forth with one hand wide.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to devise a method for returning the hand: if it cannot be returned, then raise the woman and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, spread out the legs forcefully; then bring the mustard that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, study to return the hand; and pull the child according to its natural shape, and make it vomit, and command her to hold herself as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the birth of the child on its neck, and if it has spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the bailiff hold his hand, then he turns it slowly and gently, and when it is equal, he puts natural musk on high altitude oil on it as we have said, then he commands it to move slowly; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to grab it; and make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way, support her all the second time.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it comes to be delivered in this manner completely, you press the delivery against your nail until the moisture is voided; and if the baby swells upon her face and neck, you strike from the buttocks so that it is not retained, and the infant dies; then push the child in as far as you need, and command the woman to grab it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born frequently and sometimes even four; and this is not strange and does not happen rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 These are strange things that do not live unless they are named; I know that they multiply and become desperate by the one who conceives them, which is linked to filth; and sometimes they issue out naturally like worms under a skin, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they issue forcefully, the cure is as we have said, and let the balm be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do so as it is worth moving to salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the third or fourth or fifth or sixth or seventh or more, up to fifteen, and they are all shaped like a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the balm knows all this, for by chance similar things happen; do so according to what is required.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat the woman for a dead child or miscarriage, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out by itself and you are compelled to manual labor; then you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fears death; then the woman should lie on her back with her hips inclined downward and her legs raised; and the minister should press her two parts, or tie her to the bed so she is not treated in the removal of the child; then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oils mixed with musk and fenugreek seeds and linen seed, then anoint the hands of the minister with these oils and these musks; then push gently into the woman, ensuring that she pushes out the afterbirth where it should come, and be careful that the child is not appearing at her head; if the afterbirth appears in her womb, vagina, mouth, palate, under her beard or in the navel or near the sides, or near the costal areas, then pierce it or pinch it and press it gently to the middle ribs; and hold the afterbirth with your right hand, and place the curved instrument between your left hands, and push gently into any of the places we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty state; and this is the shape of the afterbirth:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then push against each other one by one, as needed, so that the extraction is equal; and then adjust them equally by moving from side to side to make them move out, and grind them down to keep them in place, as shown in this figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if part remains, the doctor oil some of his fingers and thrusts them into that part and pulls out the other; and if none remains, place the splint or higher up in its place, and do this until it all comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be returned due to constriction, you should roll up the cloth over it until it comes out completely; then bend it at the joint of the foot or the ankle, and do this for both hands and feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is narrow at the exit, or if there is a narrow opening of the skull assembled, you must insert the pointed spatula between your fingers, and press the skull and extract the pressure; or you may use the instrument called "almidach", from which the forms come with the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and in the same way proceed if the child has a large natural swelling; then pull the bones apart using pliers, and if the head leaps out and is held back by force, it may be split as necessary until the pressure that is in the narrower position is released; and if it cannot come out, you must cut it into pieces where you can. If it is swollen in the belly or beneath the ribs, you must pierce it until the pressure subsides.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, it is a light attraction, and the direction towards the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is strained in the abdomen or thigh, you should straighten it with the cloth rolled up on your hand; and making the abdomen or thigh, correct the strains that are there; and if the other members are dislocated, and the joint remains, put the ball of your hand into the deep part of the wound, and draw it out to the mouth of the wound; then put in oil or egg yolk, and draw it further; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed due to an abscess that has come there, you should not work on it, but instead administer moist and fat substances; and administer ointments, and apply them with warm softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the infant is on its side, and you can straighten it, do as we have said in the living child's case; and if there is no power to do so, draw it apart into pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done this, apply as we have said in abscesses that come in marriage; and if bleeding comes forth, it should be put in a sharp restraint, and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman whose womb had been dead due to an infant being born, then another one was placed on top of it, and the death of the other was prevented.  (This line is referring to the survival of a second fetus after the first fetus died in the womb)
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came into the armpit, and swelled until it opened, and began to suppurate greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for treatment, and for a long time, I could not heal the wound.   (Literal translation)
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong adhesive plaster, and an bone came out, and after some days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly because the stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I think it is the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I wish to treat the wound, and take out many bones as long as the woman is in the best condition; and the woman may remain thus for a long time, and later, a small amount of pus comes from the wound; and I have no recollection of this chapter being useful except when the master finds something foreign, which he knows how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the dislocated joint back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, by which books are weighed; and at two turns, the heads of the two links.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 The cornels should be more delicate for the restrainer, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the rod should be wide, and the margin of the trees must be, and a half palm in length; and between the two limbs there should be two joints of the same rod, which should be closed on one side and the other, half a palm in length or slightly more; and these two joints are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, similar but more delicate and lighter in appearance, should be made of rod of ebony or boxwood, similar to pliers; and have two joints for the shoulders, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you are ready to open the marrow with the whole tool, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and legs apart, then insert the two joints together into the marrow, and hold the handle of the tool between her thighs; then work your hand with the whole tool, as you have done with pliers, according to the amount you want to open the mouth of the marrow, until the girl does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is covered and multiplied in their similarity; and when the mirrors have arranged them, the work becomes more urgent, and higher for humans due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disperse the instrument unless you have arranged it, for its necessity cannot be excused.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, it is necessary to instruct the patient to retain her afterbirth, and then make her vomit bile, and hold your hands at her mouth and nose; if she jumps due to this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If it is not good, take the purgative and the pot or basin, put herbs that can open the mouth of the deceased, such as rue, anise, camomile, cassia, centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a string or a basin from the pot and the other end into the mouth of the deceased, and hold it until the vapors enter the body of the deceased; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then immediately apply the second one.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment, and does not heal as commanded, instruct the woman to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or musk of aloes, then apply it to nature and wait; when she has found it, take it and stretch it gently straight, so that the man does not resist extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then draw it out; it will come and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 If the opening of the man's anus is stretched (as in a tear), we have mentioned the cure for cleaning and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not heal as described, ensure that you do not force extraction; but it is necessary that he who is at the man's opening ties himself to the woman's thigh, then anoint with ointment four-formula; when she can bear it and returns, it will heal; however, when she comes back, if there is bad smell coming from her stomach and head, and burning of the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary to use suitable fumigation for this: no one has proved fumigation of dill and dried figs in the past.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and the afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it is like glass-looking substance resembling a dog's head, and the neck is made thin in its nature, and the shoulders are wide over the fire; and let there be fumigation over the coals, and the tar until it is ruined, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born without a pierced foundation, but it is stopped up with some subtle plaster; therefore you must cut open the plaster at the appropriate time, and do not cut it with a sharp spatula, and be careful that it does not touch the foundation; then place moist linen on it in wine and oil, then anoint it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not reform, then put or pierce a plaster of lead, and let it remain for many hours, and remove it when the wound appears to heal in rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this sudden swelling of wound or abscess comes; it must be covered. If it is healed, it should be treated with the lead plaster as we have said.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodules, and those that come out from the side of the foundation swell, or in the space between two parts, if it is one fistula or more; and when that nodule becomes old, it opens, and moisture makes it white or thin boils, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; they are recognized by those who know because there is either discharge or windiness when the patient has a discharge, and in some cases, water gushes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it is fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; they reach up to the knee joint, and up to the navel of the cow.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one recognizes the persistent fistula at its base, not persisting; and it is that you bite your thumb or the base, and bite a fine awl of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twist.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 If there is a twist, then insert a thin splint or horsehair until you feel the splint or hair at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and it does not cause pus discharge, wind or water, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is open up to the bladder or up to the channel of urine, if it gushes out urine and cannot be sealed with medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is pierced up to the joint of the calf, then the splint comes up to the level; if there is no twist and the pain disappears around it, it remains thus, and neither medicine nor salve by ointment works for it; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure but labor and folly of fools who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In a woman who is neither paralyzed nor old, seeking health through iron, as I have experienced, and the patient lies prone between your hands on their back; lift their legs up to their thighs, and have their thighs inclined towards their stomach; then push a tent of iron or wood, if there is tortuosity, until you know where the hernia comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the foundation, then you must push your index finger there, if you feel that the hernia has been pierced; and uncover or find where the intestine or flesh is, then know that it is paralyzed; do not move it as one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 One should know that one can heal some things, but it happens rarely; and the aid one gives, it is this: heat the cautery subtle according to the width of the fistula, as before said; and push it all hot into the fistula, until it comes out from the base; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred things should be burned, which are similar to a feather of an eye; and then heal with wet bandages in butter, until that char is gone, then heal with ointment soothing and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed otherwise and if it swells up and does not perforate the hole which is at its base, put a thick cover of leather or fabric between your finger and the swelling, so that you can see the fistula under the covering of the finger; then strike from the beginning of the fistula, push forward the swelling first, and then the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the end of the swelling; and the swelling will be released and charred; then remove those charred things which are like a feather of a bird, and let none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the limb goes away by itself, and breaks through [the skin], you shall cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The fire cautery brings about two good things: the burning of these sores joined together, and the stopping of blood and removal of moisture; then it heals wounds filled with moistened tents made of butter or crushed cheese until the flesh hardens, and it treats the wound with dry ointments.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	And when it is restored, it heals and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	If a fistula comes up to the full depth of the foundation and is removed from the body, push your finger or foundation into it, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent, and between them is cloth or lining or sores that are close to piercing, there should be no opening except for a way of trust and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods: you can cauterize it as we have said, or you can cut it down to the bottom, or if you can, put on tents and heal it as before; do not go too deep that you cover the foundation holding structure, and let the purulence come out by its own will; then heal it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it is cut away from the bottom, either through a tent or another instrument appointed for it; then remove the infected tissue in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part furthest from the foundation: it will be easier on the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas are formed in this manner: when you bite the tent (?) into the fistula and it is on the side close to the foundation beneath the skin above, take a punctured tent (?) at the top in this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert one twisted thread into two, and push the tent with the whole length of the thread through the fistula as far as it reaches on the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it persists on the side of the foundation inside, then draw out the thread of that punctured tent (?), and bite your tooth or foundation into it; pull out the head of the thread, and bring together the two ends, and bind them together, and hold one against the other, and leave it for a day or two; hold it once in a while until the threads touch those things between them and close up (?); then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst on its own, make it burst in all possible ways, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it should not be covered with a plaster if it is too deep, and then heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the spur-like spinous part from which the fistula is made is very sharp at one end and blunt on the other; and yet it should not be struck where it should not be struck, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 There are two kinds of emorrhoids: those that are inside the base, like a piece of resin, and have both small and large ones, with blood coming from them, and they have one or more, and are turned away from the base and at the top of the base; but those that are turned away have some moisture, and there is either a little or a lot of clear citron juice or blood, and have the color of the body; and the treatment for these that have them inside the base, it is that you instruct the patient to strain for urination in bed, until the bases become visible, and the filaments appear; then hurry and clip them with scissors, or hold with your nail, then strike at their roots; and if the filaments cannot be held due to moisture, take cotton or lint, or a piece of camel's hair; and bind them with your hands, then strike, and sprinkle hot powders on top, such as those used for cautery; or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cautery, afterwards curing them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the bases cannot come out, instruct the patient to be clisterized with a sharp and biting clisterium for washing the affected area, so that it comes out easily; when the patient strains, and the filaments are visible at the base, the treatment is easy; and it is that you take them with your nail or scissors, strike them, and cure as we have said, until they are healed, and that the patient fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You must perform the stitching in this manner: take twisted thread and put it on a needle, then draw the thread above and pierce the needle from another side; then turn the two ends of the thread below the needle and make them as wide as necessary; tie the thread securely, then untie it, remove the needle, and do the same with all the others; leave the excess for the blood to drain; place a damp linen cloth soaked in rose oil or resin on the wound foundation, and place it there, and command the patient to rest; then let it heal until it scabs over, and when they have fallen off, treat them with ointment and other cures until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	the drying of the wounds or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often the drying of wounds occurs in the intestines due to natural constriction and when the disease is old and medicine no longer helps.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you cauterize the tip of a splinter or your nail with a knife, so that it does not get wet; then cure it until it heals as needed; and if it cannot heal, you should shave more strongly than before, until it drains pus and is scabbed over; then cure it until it heals.
dou fremit	great trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Fissure is a small opening in the body, and it extends deep within; sometimes it affects the frostbite, and it feels as if death is near, and it spreads throughout the body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure for this is to take a reed from an ostrich feather, or a strong quill, and place that reed on the frostbite until the purple circle encloses it completely; then turn your hand around the entire reed so that you cover all of the frostbite, push it in deep, and remove the frostbite from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a chain made of iron or steel according to this form, and be careful beneath and pull above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce (it), to keep the tooth in place, and press it. And if you wish, cauterize the limb as described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of a clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times, they make a silver or arsenic enema, or molten lead or mercury, and at times they make such small and large instruments, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when it is used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and suffering, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema, whether it is large or small, should be above wide, or the belly should be bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And it should have an opening where the belly is sewn, as you see, and the shoulders should be pierced within; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other one; and put inside the belly the medicine of a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierce all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be some space, then insert strong thread through these holes, either crosswise or in X shape, and assemble the belly like a goatskin; when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then press; this is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clistere with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the ministers should pull on both ends of the clistere until it is completely stretched out, then remove the clistere, and tie the patient's legs to the outside when the medicine appears; if it oozes out, hold it tightly as much as possible; if he sleeps all night, it will be a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize it in case of disease of the intestines, and the medicine hastens to heal, keep applying it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoid is either based or an abscess, it should be treated with a suppository as gentle as for a child; and this is the form of a gentle suppository where the skin should be stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division [section] the treatment of wounds; now we shall tell you the treatment for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places or wounds where they are made, and from how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 Things that wounds are done by are by stone cutting, sword or knife cuts, lance or arrow wound, shield-beat, or similar things; or those that are done according to the laws of the body, such as a wound on the neck, head, leg, belly, liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds in the head, since it will remind you in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound or abscess comes and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is caused by an arrow or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large; doubt the presence of an abscess warmly: let it drain immediately from the head itself if blood comes from the wound, and let it drain to the opposite side of the damaged part; and let the patient evacuate repletion with wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it does not want to drain, let its meat be reduced, and let it not drink wine, nor eat any fat; and put on the wound, if an abscess hot comes, dampened wool in rose oil only, or in vinegar steeped; and if there is no hot abscess, put fresh linen on the wound, all its blood, and it is not moved by air, a small amount of powder, which I will say a little later; and if the fire has moved it, put some onions on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a sword and cannot be closed with stitches, join them by sewing, as I will explain for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed of the bone, and opens, and does not hold but only a little, close it; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large foods such as cooked heads (testes) and wheat, also like peas, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find pus or rotten skin on the bone, and it does not reach the bone, then cut off the entire pus and throw away, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped without surgery, and it does not stop bleeding with medicines, then try to stop the artery; and if you find the artery dislocated, tie it up with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy; it is that you put this powder on it so that the arrows have stuck.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the way of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; three parts live coal and grind finely, then apply to the wound, press it firmly until it ventilates well and joins with all its blood; then tie it well, and leave it to heal if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes they do this with just boiling water, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the wound has not yet opened.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the fire has burned the wound, it should be treated immediately without using this powder; instead, apply some appropriate remedies such as a paste made of barley flour and water or honey, until it stops oozing; then heal it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if a bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with subtle forceps; and I will tell you afterwards about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	Of the collar wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes from the neck and it is simple, without a difference between it and the one on the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it's nerves, there should be no other tool but to let them heal naturally and not apply anything restricting, as this harms the nerves and causes them to retreat; do not put anything cold on the wound, since nerve substance is cold, and its growth continues with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as water boiled in sweet vinegar and mixed with rose oil, heated water treated likewise in sweet vinegar, and other similar things moistened.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, tie it up with strips, then treat it until it heals.
