Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and she is swollen and full of pus, pierce or pierce lower; and if the arteries are cut, and bleeding comes out, stop it, and lance, cauterize if necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is kept, so that the meat goes through the windpipe, and does not touch the windpipe but put it back according to its natural shape; then hold it straight, and let it stay for some days, then treat with scented ointments until it heals; and if the wound has pressed against the bone, drill; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out as you can, and those that you cannot have, leave until the wound festers, and let the pus issue and heal the opening; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on it as I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of a wound from a lance or knife   (This line suggests that the text is discussing treatments for wounds inflicted by weapons.)
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a sword or knife wound and the wound is deep, check if the patient's breath comes quickly from the wound: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and the wound is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at first hour, nor bind it for the blood that will clot completely, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but apply attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound 3 or 4 days, or more; there will be no spasm, nor bad tremors of heart or other signs of pain; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat the disease and other remedies as long as he is healthy; if it cannot heal, and an opening occurs, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as it should be treated.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is a sword or knife incision, and it is simple or worse, or at the back, treat it according to what is in front of it; if it is large, stitch it; if it is small, apply powder, and if it has penetrated the bone, remove the pieces as necessary, and pull out the protruding pieces if they are dislocated; if they are not dislocated, let the wound heal by itself and align the extractions. And for other wounds on various limbs, the judgment is according to what we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The first dismemberment of the abdomen is large, medium, and small; from a large wound, any intestines occasionally protrude, or the intestine's layers, due to which the insertion is difficult; and suturing is more troublesome, and often a small wound is worse than a large one because it requires more care when replacing the intestines in; since the intestines inflate suddenly when they feel cold, they return more easily, and therefore a medium-sized wound is preferable; since it is necessary to repair moved intestines to their place rather than other ones. And you should know that the incision of the abdomen follows four ways: the two common sutures in the abdominal incision, and the sutures of other body wounds, as well as other specific ones are common for other wounds; but they are more related to the abdominal suture, and I will explain each one individually.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines protrudes from it, it is easily set, this is by one of the two methods: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or dampen a cloth in hot water only, or you cook in hot squill and cyperus and spike, and anoint the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes make this wine-restraining, and it is moved that away to deswell.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling separate, if you moisten the intestines with hot or warm water and bitter herbs are cooked, for in this way the entrance is opened a little; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision at the instrument with which emorrhoids are struck; and the first cure is to cut that away, for we should not cut too much unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument for breaking: slice within the cavity and do not push out, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines leap out, put them back in place according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power to do so, for it is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the part beneath the stomach, you must make the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part beneath the stomach, raise the head and buttocks higher than the parts beneath; and in the same way, when the abdomen is torn in one of the two halves, pay attention to making the damaged side higher than the other; and in this way, administer as I say for large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 Small wounds should be treated with what suits you, then have a compassionate person who anoints the entire wound with his hand and pinches it shut; and this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or more than one, according to the width of the wound, then leave space from the edge of the wound and pierce it with a needle where it has good strong thread; and pierce the two layers of skin with the two layers of flesh beneath, which is under the skin inside, as far as you make it pierce from that side, and gather the four edges together; then tie a double thread around the needle in two parts, then gather the two sides of the wound together and leave space, and pierce another needle; then bind the thread as you did with the first needle and do not stop doing this according to what is needed for needles, until the entire wound is tied; and the needles should be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, because thin needles pierce all the flesh and large ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be medium-sized. And it is not good to push the needles too far away from the flesh and skin so that they do not injure and open the wound before it is sewn; and then tie the heads of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and place threads or cloth around the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. This method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires one needle or two assisting needles for larger wounds; and when you have pierced all four edges together, remove the needle to the part where you started, in the manner they cut cloth. I sewed a wound on a man who had a stomach, which was wounded with a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and his intestines were well two palms wide, and the wound was inside the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestine when it had been twenty-four hours away, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and it was cured, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 They had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; I did not treat him with any salve, because I was at a place where none were found nor any medicine; and I placed cotton old twice a day over the wound, and washed it with water of honey until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle, and insert it from one side to the other; when it has pierced through straight in straight, then place the tip of the skin or hide where you inserted the needle, and pierce it from the other side from inside out; and the meaning of this stitching is that you sew as the pelletier sews fur, and leave a gap once, and take it up again, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of stitching, which Galen calls specifically, is done in the same way by those who assemble the two parts naturally and apply one head of the needle to the other, following this method: drive a needle or the point of the mirror through that place only, leaving the two heads of the needle; then turn the needle, and drive it from the outer part towards the inner, into the two heads of the needle; then drive it from the outer part towards the inner, into the two other heads of the mirror on the opposite side; and this is the moving method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens said this word and it is true, one should stitch the stomach with two needles, having thread in each; one needle must be driven from one side and the other from the opposite, in the manner of those who sew sacks; and know that when the incision is inside the stomach, the stitching is more severe than in other parts of the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgement of the wound is similar to that of other wounds: it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, as soon as the arrow has moved it, you should put back the intestines and skin; then put powder-healing char on top, and if the arrow has moved, you should put any ointment available on top until the wound heals over; suture the flesh, bind it with threads, and let it heal; then care for the wound as for other wounds, until it is healthy; and if you don't have medicines, put old cotton on it, and stir it two times a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 You do not need any other medicine in many situations when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound infects the principal members, it is necessary to moisten light linen with warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the swellings, and under the saddle; and if pain or corruption occurs in the bowels, and this happens often, clisterize with black wine that is warm, and also when the corruption comes up to the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "yew" cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is due to the planting of veins in them, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the hernia jumps out of the wound, put it back in place as one would with an intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned or blackened, you should cut away the black part, so that no blood flow comes, because there are veins and arteries; then take hold of what is between the hernia sac, and hang both heads hanging from the part below the wound to facilitate extraction when the hernia falls out, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, as I have seen a man pierced or stabbed by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, with discharge and flatulence; I cured it according to what I knew, and did not stop refining until it healed, and the edges sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I see it stitched, I suspected that the patient had illness in his stomach; but there was no illness, but he improved in better condition, and ate and drank; and any experimentor said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied up in this manner: take deep breaths with large bellows, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the breath has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches out; and then strike the head, and hold it so it cannot dislocate, then put another breath after in the same manner until the wound is completely closed; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head (of an injury or lesion) becomes swollen inside the intestine and brings no harm to the patient, it can be stitched with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the end of this intestinal thread which is sharpened, then tie it to the head of a thread of flax twisted together, then insert the thread into a needle, and sew up the intestine and tie it off; and this method of stitching should not be far from faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no trick or healing, but rather depends on subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or when it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called "fistula", and equally when it opens and swells up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And fistula is according to truth a hard and white nodule, in which there is no pain, and is as swollen as the feather of a bird; and sometimes it clearly pops open, and at other times thickens; sometimes it is small, and at other times quite large; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is otherwise by one of the nine causes: namely, because of the small amount of blood or body heat; or due to its malicious nature; or because there is hard flesh within, and above the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or it has too much pus; or the place is pushed in, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or it is a corruption that is like pestilence; or due to the property of the region, digestion is slow and health is late and festering by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you the cure for fistula that is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or intestines, bladder, ribs, spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and sometimes they come to the property of the main member and similar parts.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing except labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have mentioned, and you have confidence in its cure, and you know it, take a tent of honey or iron, if the fistula is straight, pierce it; and if the fistula is twisted, look for a thin probe of wood, because wood bends with the twists; and if the fistula has been punctured and you cannot find it by probing, cleanse it through one of the punctures, because moisture flows from one puncture to another and cleanses it; then pierce it skillfully as far as your power allows, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and whether it is completely healed, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is distant from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the places I have mentioned, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the damaged tissue and corrupt matter that are inside; and then heal it as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is well located in the right place, you must cut completely, as far as you can, then put moistened bandages soaked in medicinal oil into it, and push them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous matter that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments made of clean fat into it, until it is healed; and if it does not heal by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If no vein or nerve is affected nor the principal members [are], as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove the corruption as much as possible, then treat with things antiseptic until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns swollen as before, know that you are not done yet: expose and cut as deep as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep, you cannot reach it; if there is only a little corrupted bone, and you can extract it with the pliers, remove it according to the situation suitable for that bone, and if there are many bones, extract them all, do not leave any one behind; and if moisture prevents you or there is error or fear, strike and push back moisture and the pus, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove [the foreign object] within an hour, put something irritating pus on the wound and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will be easier to extract; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, press down on the corruption only until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of rot and it reaches the bone marrow, you must remove and cover everything up to the corruption, then heal it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was about thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, such that materials came into the leg, and he developed a large abscess, and there was no suitable place to open it; but they foolishly opened the abscess repeatedly, causing much drainage of materials, and it became a fistula, and much pus flowed out that all went bowel and moisture from the body; and many fools tried to cure him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine until I was summoned, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was leaking through the sores at great cost; and the body of the young man turned red, and had a citrus-like color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I inserted a tent in one of the wounds, and then I sought all the wounds, and found that some came towards the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I then hurried and cut in one of the wounds as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and broken, and corruption was coming towards the bone from within; I saw the corrupted part of the bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for what remained; and I began to heal the wound with healing salves for a long time, but it would not heal; then I tried again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and it was corrupted, and I left it, and I tried to heal the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm of the bone, and removed it entirely, and then I healed it with salves; and it became healthy and healed quickly, and no further work was needed except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation often bloodied, but it became entirely healthy, and grew in the bone a hard cyst, and was of good condition and had no harm or contrary to anything at all, neither on the outside nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated thus: take thread and tie at the end of the opened bone and command someone to pull up; then place another thicker thread of linen over the cyst that is on the bone, and hold tight so that you draw out the corrupted cyst from below, and expose the cyst on the site where it should be, so as not to prick the cyst; place fire or a wedge beneath the bone to move the corrupted cyst; and must stay as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and stay further times.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, you should remove all the flesh; then place the iron under it, and then press from one side to the other the corrupted part, as we have said; and if the corruption is at a joint, you should break the corrupted joint, and the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy but to cut it; and if the corruption is at the tip of the hand or foot, it is a very difficult matter, but nevertheless you must investigate the corruption and how it opens; and clean it in all possible ways, but do not harm the vein or nerve; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the type of bone and its appearance, and its thickness and its subtlety, and its size and smallness, and its hardness; and therefore you must prepare an instrument for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to the understanding of this art, and the experience of the types of diseases; and think about the tool you need in accordance with what is required.
dou feu	Hot iron
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulder may dislocate either internally or externally; and when you have medicine to treat this corruption by the means of medicines, but it does not improve, it is necessary to cover that member up to where the corruption begins, so that the patient escapes from death due to this defect of the limb, or from the greater evil, the lack of function in the member; and the signs are that the limbs become black, as if burned by fire, and afterwards it turns black, because the corruption of the member spreads from one to another and takes over the entire body; act quickly to cover it, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous animals such as sea scorpion, viper and similar, if the corruption is at the head of the hand, cover it, do not give it any space to reach up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it comes up to the hand, strike it at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, strike at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no remedy outside the quantity of its virtue can help; and thus you do when the corrosion comes or in the foot: if it comes in the first joint, strike after the next joint; and if it comes in the foot, strike the entire foot; and if it goes up to the leg, strike at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than letting the patient die; and the method of striking or searing the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister on the lower chain, and another minister on the upper chain, and you sever the flesh that is between the two chains with a spatula wide enough so that the bone is exposed; then strike or sear, and place linen cloths on either side, so that the searing does not touch healthy skin, and brings the patient further injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding comes when you work, cauterize the area promptly, or apply certain powders to restrain; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb with a suitable ligature, and cure it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my time: there was a blackness resembling fire burn, and this corruption first came upon his foot, consuming all the foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he covered the foot with copper, and it healed; and a long time later the corruption returned to his toe or his hand, and it came to me, and I treated him with medicines after cleansing of the body, but the corruption did not stop; and he asked that I amputate his hand, and I refused, for I had hope to cure the matter; and I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired, returned to his earth, and covered his hand with copper, and it healed; and I have not told this story except for this reason: one does otherwise if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Aposteme sometimes comes in charnut place and remains for so long that it causes a large swelling of the bowels; then it turns and perforates, and the bowel leaps out, staying visible like a vassal's; and the skin above is as delicate as unbleached linen and does not reach the bone or the nerve. Such disease is called "sain" and not "fistule"; but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone in full, it is called "fistule"; and the skin should be cut around it, just like unbleached linen; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	1. And if the skin hardens and the corruption is not complete, and the flesh is thick with pus, cure it with a poultice in this way: Look to see if the breasts are large, and the sore that is within them stinks; then apply an Egyptian-made poultice which is made thus: Take asafetida, oil, litharge, equally, cook them in a pot over fire until the medicine becomes red and thick like honey; then take as needed from this, make it into water and honey, and apply the poultice to the breast, and tighten the wound; leave the poultice for two hours, then remove it by unwrapping; do this many times, until the breasts are healed, and the pus is expelled; and sometimes poultice with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and take vine ash, pour water over it, then apply the poultice, until you know that the breasts are well healed; and if the patient cannot endure it, or the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, poultice with water and honey or mead, so that the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the blood thicken; and when you have done this, and you are certain that the breasts are well cleaned, poultice with whatever grows new flesh in them, and take emplaster of roses and oil; or poultice with various medicines and ointments, whose properties I have told you before treating sores; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the cloth of the poultice cannot enter, widen it a little with an iron, and place a piece of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment over it, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, cover it and leave only enough space for the poultice to enter, and if the sore smells foul, press down or lower it somewhat.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the bowel is fully expanded, do not let any air enter it; and if you cannot cover the belly under it as you see, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves to its lowest position, for when the bowel is fully expanded, do not let any air enter it and if you cannot cover the belly under it as you see. Arrange it in this way: the bowel moves lightly downwards, do not leave anything from the bowel; take medicines that consolidate and put them on the wound, and place a linen cloth over the entire wound; then press strongly towards the injured side more to the right than the first time, as there is already an opening there, and bind again with another cloth according to the size of the injury, and place it on the injured side to align the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days once; and the one who is on the injured side, often removes to remove the bowel, and recognize what comes from the bowel, whether it is poison or pus or undigested or indigestible. Take care that the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread out in this way and you see the nature that arises on the injured side, then recognize that the bowels have opened and approach health; and then unbind it in the morning, or the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the binding.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts sag due to indigestion after many days, know that they will not correct themselves.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poison spreads for a long time, do not despair of health, because health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For those who suffer from pus in their wounds and those who do the opposite; and if he swells his breast indigest for many days, know that the breasts do not swell; and if the breasts are slow to heal and are hardened, use drying medicines with a dry substance and moist virtues, such as oil of roses, equal parts of old wine, mix it together and boil it, and then apply it; and when oils of roses are not present, take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire, and then apply it to the cloth and place it on the breast, and sometimes administer an aromatic long oil and celestial roots, which is also like flour and centaury; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make into powder, and add to the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the wound is deep and not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has spread throughout, and causes pressure on the bone, or hard tissues, or ligaments; cure it with the cure of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess at the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Parasitic abscess is a boil that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, and sometimes appears in other places; and when it matures without care being taken, if it is left untreated, it causes a contagious boil to spread, running and exuding pus until it reaches the root of the nail, possibly destroying it completely; and the corrosion reaches the bone, causing pain that smells foul, and the joints become large and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When treating it as we have previously mentioned in the section, and if the treatment does not help, you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great aid if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to swell and inflame, it is necessary that you place the iron under the nail so as not to touch the flesh, and push upwards, gently and lightly striking the inflamed area; then apply the remaining charred and corrosive substances on top to remove all of it; afterwards, heal it with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 If the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and draw it out, because as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; if you see that it needs to be corrected, strike it with a sharp spatula as described before, then heal it until it heals; and if it is wounded and hurts a lot, it is necessary to first heal it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula in a transverse manner, but ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, place something on top to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The deafening pain of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 One must align the fingers that are born in some men by chance, which are entirely flesh and sometimes contain tendons or bones, and occasionally nails; and none of these grow from the root of a joint, but they grow in some parts of the hand or in the knuckles.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one who grows from any finger in the hand does not move, and the one who grows at a joint of the hand, by chance may move; the size of the fleshy one is slight, as follows: cut it off at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	One who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: keep yourself covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who grows or should grow in the last finger, it is necessary that you cut the round part up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and cure it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Simultaneously, swelling in the joints comes from birth, or from injury of the wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If it is necessary to seal that wound, let it heal according to its natural shapes; then place between two tents or dampened cloths in oil of roses, so they do not stick together; or you may place between two thin pieces of wood until the edges are sealed as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of its two (joints) comes with the palm, then strike that weld as necessary.
des vils	 of the simple folk
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 These are large veins filled with melancholic superfluities that come in many parts of the body; and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should sometimes administer purge of bile, and then heal the basilica (abdomen).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The iron cure is of two kinds: the first is to seal it and draw out black blood; and the second kind is that you tie the vein and let all the blood out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The shape of the incision is as follows: first, heat a sharp and very hot knife, until the flesh becomes soft, then hold the patient's leg above the knee to the lower part of the thigh; then make an incision in I, II or III position, large in size, then separate and draw out black blood up to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the sickness can bear; and then bind it, and order the patient to eat foods with stimulating dark wine; and repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and this is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The swelling is as follows: raise the patient's leg, if there is much hair on it, then put it in warm water, and heat the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins become swollen; and if you do not have warm water, heat it over fire, and then strike it near the long part of the thigh or below the knee; then peel off the skin at the edge, and scrape the vein from both sides, as far as it appears; and you will see it red and black, and when it comes out or the skin seems like a white cord; then push the fat down, until it is raised above the skin, and then cut it lightly along the edge, then strike another incision in another place within III fingers; then peel off the skin over the vein as far as it appears, then draw it out to the fat, as you have done, and make another incision, as you did before; then make another cut, or more if necessary, then draw it out, and cut it at the end of the foot, then pull and draw it up to the second cut; then remove it piece by piece, until it is all drawn out, then cut it; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, put a double-threaded needle through it all along, tie and draw it, and push it down under the fat, and turn your hand from one side to another, until it comes out; and be careful not to cut, as if it cuts, you cannot draw it out or lift it, and this is harmful to the patient; and when you have completely treated it, put linen soaked in wine and oil on the wound site; and cure it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is constricted, twisted and rolled together, and it's not straight as we have said, then you must break it forcefully but do not cover it; pull it as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to break the face should be curved, but not thin, so it does not pierce the vein; and it should be large because if it is fine, it will pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	 Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is inserted in the legs, in hot areas where no grass or tree grows and in dry ground; and by chance it may grow elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to corruption that comes from under the skin, as it comes within the body serpents and worms and penetrates between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very large swelling in the leg, then the flesh changes and the vein begins to protrude, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the thigh is opened, you should wrap around it a piece of plank about 7 to 8 inches long and bind it, leaving the plank on the leg; every time it starts to ooze, you should re-wrap around the plank and bind it again; if it is too long, cut off a part, re-wrap the remaining and do not cover its root, because if you cover it, it returns into the flesh, causing abscesses, corruption and illness; so it must be treated gradually until it reaches the groin and there remains nothing on the body; sometimes this vein, when treated, can be up to 5 or 10 feet long, and once I had a patient whose vein was 10 feet long, and when you cut it, it bursts out with pus or blood, and you should empty the material inside, introduce medicines for abscesses every day, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein, many injuries occur, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or hand, and there is much damage, and it jumps around; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 The worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, moving and swelling throughout the body, causing pain in the joints of the limbs as it goes, tearing the skin where it passes, and jumping out; it is caused by the corruption of certain humors, such as those found in snakes and lizards and tapeworms or intestines; there is suspicion about its harmful effects, for when it moves through the body and reaches the head, it can enter the oil and destroy it; this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to be treated and drained, one can force it out only when it moves: therefore, you must lie the limb above and below with a strong cord tightly tied; then strike on top and pull it out, and if its opening is completely in the flesh and you cannot feel it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it causes is that it bursts oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold a spoon-shaped instrument beneath it, then strike on top and pull it out; and the patient must use body purification of medicines soluble for evil humors, and avoid consuming foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 The pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" on our land, and it is a pain that moves from one member to another. I have seen this happen as I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and when I examined her arm, I saw a small swelling in the armpit; and shortly after, it began to rise like a worm at the shoulder, faster than anything else, as sharp silver cuts from one place to another; the pain left that place and lodged in the shoulder, then ran quickly through all over the body, until it came to the other arm; then she said that it returned around the body again, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 All in all, I wished that many who wanted to move pain from one place to another had not wished this, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought this was because the woman had a dry body, and veins uncovered, and for this reason these constricted windiness appeared; and it is not the case according to this reasoning for those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and veins hidden.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to cure this disease and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, lay it above and below quickly, then strike above so that this constricted windiness leaves at the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, cure it with those who expel the windiness, such as fetid pills, pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	 arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 There are various types of arrows, some with large points, small, pointed or blunt, and some with two tips, others with tongues, and those that have splinters; and when one of these falls into any member it falls in one of two ways: either into a principal member like the head, heart, liver, stomach, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it falls into any place of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you afterwards appear, you must be careful about the extraction of this arrow, for death comes in many ways; and when this illness does not show signs or the arrow is not completely embedded, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.
