And the sign of the brain when an arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and the skull swells up above the brain, is when there is scotomia (partial or complete loss of vision), scod (blackening or purplish discoloration), esvertin (convulsions), roujor (redness) in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of the mind, vomiting of bile; and perhaps without fever from the nose or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and swelling appears from the wound white like pus, and also as bubbling of pus; and if this sign is apparent, avoid treatment, and pull out the arrow if it isn't in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of an arrow wound when it pierces or strikes the chest is that it is near the left breast, and feels like it has been thrust into a hard object, not empty; and by chance the arrow may also swell up as the fingers do, and produce black cold blood, and chills and cold sweats, and fainting: hence there can be no doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that penetrates the flesh deeply is when there is no scum discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, breathes heavily and seeks a warm place.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the cover of the mattress, it should be removed through the small openings; and you must release great pain and great suffering and groans; and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, by chance, something of indigestible meat may jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly or abdomen, and does not jump out through the intestinal route, there is no hope in the cure nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and loin and hips and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it does not move, as I will tell you what happened to me, for this reason that you do the following:
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow pierced or struck his neck at the root: I pulled it out from the other side beneath the ear fat, and it was healthy without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And pulled out an arrow that pierced the oil gland beneath the paper below, and the arrow was round, and could not be grasped except by the tip towards the body, and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bow, entirely sharp at both ends; the youth remained unharmed, and no harmful accident occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And draw an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I was beardless, and sharpened it until I drew it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And draw an arrow that was stuck in a man, whether in his head or belly, and I thought he would die; but after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, tricked it, drew it out, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if a man has an arrow fall on his back or spine, and the wound is sewn up; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not alter his natural conditions, nor causes harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And to another man, a arrow struck him in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and he endured so for a long time suffering great pain; and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And to the man of the princes, the king, who fell among the snow and was slightly sloping towards the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was summoned for his treatment after he had fallen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I pierced it with a very fine needle and did not feel it myself; but he felt prickling and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the arrowhead. I put on the right side a plaster adhesive and absorbent, because the side did not swell; and the arrowhead appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I placed the emplastrum (medical ointment or paste) on [the wound] for several days, and straightened the wound directly, and the patient stayed like that for a long time until he felt the arrow within his flesh; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 For several days, I applied the corrosive medicine over the wound until it opened, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow protruding from its place; then I applied the medicine corrosive around the opening of the wound for several months, until the tip of the arrow became visible; and after more than four months had passed, the wound that I stitched with pliers could not heal; so I did not stop trying to find ways with various tools, until I made the pliers properly according to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, as I drew it out, and returned the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the men judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored; I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was entirely well.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 And I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, but do not take my word for it completely, because books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters understand a little about many things, and in dealing with what is present and failing, they reveal new work, and they invent nine tools, to the removal of foreign bodies which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not leave the body where they are lodged except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or from another side; and one which jumps out at the place where it enters is called an arrow in the flesh, and sometimes jumps out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, leave it until the flesh is swollen around it and the opening is wide; and similarly, if it is pierced in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for some days, and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it still does not jump, perforate it all around with a sharp instrument until the area around it is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 If the arrowhead is embedded in the bone of the skull and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, or any of the accidents I have mentioned earlier: do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even after some days, because if the arrow comes as far as the subdural space, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not driven deep into the bone only and does not reach to the surface, and the patient remains for some days with bad condition, then try to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it (the arrow) is deeply embedded and cannot be removed, administer tourniquets around it as I told you, then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 If the arrow is lodged within the body so that it cannot be seen, try to find it with all your efforts; if you feel it, try to draw it out with any implement available; if you cannot do so due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then enlarge the wound as much as possible; draw the arrow out if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow like they hold on, remove the flesh that is embedded in two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can draw it out; be careful not to break the arrow while doing so, but try to draw it out gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot dislocate it once, push the leg towards the joint, then draw it, for extraction will be easier in this case.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood hinders you, apply what we have said in its chapter for treatment; and beware of incising the nerve or vein, and use an apparatus to draw out the arrow as safely as possible, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to how he was when the arrow struck him, because this is the greatest aid that can be given, and if you cannot, do so according to what the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from somewhere else, or opens something with it, or the skin is swollen in that place where you can see or feel it clearly: cut then above, as far as the tongs can grasp, and then pull it out; if it jumps away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it alone for the time being and then continue the extraction until it comes forth; and if there is an arrowhead inside it, push it to its full length; and if it has fallen, and you wish to administer a cure, use pliers so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then push harder, and when the arrow is removed, push the pliers in further with the pointed end entering, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrow is touched, it is necessary to cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls into the side, chest, abdomen, bladder or ribs, and is near the surface, and you can cover it, do so; but be careful to not cut the vein or nerve, then extract it, and stitch the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The form of the buttock hair is also like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrowhead, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tweezers for pushing and testing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The number of veins from which one drains is thirty-one, of which the head is sixteen, to wit: two bladders that are after the ears, which are called the "doubles herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples apparent; and the two veins that are on the eyes, which are called "aspirées"; and the vein that is at the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two glands that are at the neck; and the two veins that are in the upper lips, and these veins are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly healed in each arm are V: one is cephalic, located on the left side of the chest and called by laymen "arm vein"; the median is called "fistula", composed of the cephalic and basilic, and laymen call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic is located on the right side of the chest and laymen call it "ventral vein" which is above the elbow and is the one through which blood is drawn, appearing manifestly at the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the cubital vein is the one between the little finger and ring finger, and it has two rain-like branches; and in the leg there are three veins: one is below the elbow on the left side of the chest, the second saphenous vein which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nase" which is at the other ankle's wrist; and in the other leg there are also three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The patient should aid the sinuses located behind the ears with old cathartics and emetics; and the quality of the sinus cleanser, as I tell you, is that you seize the head of the patient, and rub the place where the sinuses are with a harsh cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a pin until the two sinuses appear behind the ears in the two dependent places of the head: then bend down when you feel the pulse under your chin, and press firmly; then take the lancet, and push it through the sinus up to the bone, then pull your hand all along the sinus, and strike the skin and the sinus well two times through; and make the blood come out until you see; then bind and tie it until it is healed; and I have already said about the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The first artery of the two located in the temples, has the ability to drain old, soft, and common otalgia (ear pain); its properties are as I say: a patient must turn their neck so that both veins appear clearly; feel the pulse beneath your jaw, then apply pressure on it; next lift the vein up towards the neck at the indicated place, insert the lancet, lift the vein up and squeeze, just like you have done in the other veins, and release the blood according to your need; then release the patient, put your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; next, shape it (the vein) and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their treatment and extraction, which begins the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The vein of the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein in old facial diseases, and it has migrated and turned red; and its qualities are such that the patient turns his neck while twisting it until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the point on the vein, and press from above with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein when it is healthy and never stop working with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp; and slice across as the bone is near, so that the flames do not break when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The veins in the two eyelids help with eye problems, redness, swelling, and facial diseases; and the qualities of their vein are such that the patient turns his neck while twisting it from any link, as before; then tie the vein and let the traverse vein be slightly longer and wider than usual, because there is no heat involved.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break [the patient's skin]; then make a wound of blood, as much as you need, and then cover it with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The opening of the vein in the neck is useful for ague, scurvy, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that come from the face, and especially when it is old; and the qualities of the vein are that the patient squeezes his neck, then squeezes his nose with your left hand, and takes fine, long flame, and inserts it into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well anywhere else, and the pulse will begin to beat now; and do not go too deep, and make the bleeding according to your need, then stop for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The following of the two veins assists in the contraction of the aneurysm, and at the beginning of the formation of the anastomosis, and in many diseases, and ulcerations, and inflammation, and suppuration, and herpes, and strangulations; and the quality of the vein is such that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and the master standing over the head of the patient, and the patient lies on the bed, then open the long vein a little widely, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then repeat this process in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and gently tighten all the veins so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	 From the liver surgery
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The purification of veins in the mouth above helps to cool [the mouth] and promotes decay of the gums, fissures in the lips, toothache, and surrounding areas.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the liver surgery are to make the patient sit in front of you and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at the two veins, one on the right liver and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that there are smaller black veins around them: therefore strike both, and if you do not know which one it is, or if you are uncertain, strike the largest of each, and the same applies to the upper and lower veins because it is done in the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 From below the tongue liver
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The liver surgery of the veins beneath the tongue is performed after the cephalic surgery, and it is at the incision of the throat, and for diseases of the eye and mouth; and the qualities of the liver surgery are that the patient lies down with his hands between the sun, and he lifts the tongue and looks below on each side for a black vein: therefore pierce both, but do not go too deep, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins from which one commonly heals are healed in two ways: either by pricking with a large, thin instrument, such as a lance or subtle olive oil, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and fine according to the size and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirrhine is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary to open thick veins full of large, apparent blood and containing large, turbid blood; and this is the shape of olive oil flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more subtle, and it is for treating subtle veins that contain subtle, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the healer to heal quickly and for him to release the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if the artery is touched, and bleeding ensues, it must be stopped, as I have said; but the flame should not be pricked, but cut like a lance.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilica does not open manifestly, you must force it to open, and change another; or you may wish any relief from it, or you may sanction in its place the vein through the arm: it opens manifestly; and touch the flame with a lance, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to know the location of the vein, then it is necessary that you force the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the point of entry, bind the arm, and burn the vein with a lance; and beware not to wound the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is of the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it rising high like the urine of a child, and the wound is red and subtle, know that it is not from an artery: therefore hurry up, and place your finger firmly on top for a long time, then remove your finger until the bleeding stops; often this happens; if the arm is affected, leave it as it is, and do not let the patient move it; and be afraid and do not let him move it until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the artery does not appear swollen and it inflames, and there is no medicine present, cut open the artery if it is open, as the head of the wound recedes; bleed the limb.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of willow bark, cut it in half and place one part on top until the next day; if it stops bleeding, that's good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping of bleeding should not be delayed for various reasons due to the small size of the wound or the thickness of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from both the head above and the body below, because it is made up of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the healer must beware of the nerve that is underneath, and if it pricks too deep, and he finds the nerve, and inflates and the patient's condition worsens or there is no recovery; and this nerve opens up frequently, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then you must drain it with an instrument; and avoid the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The vein of the head helps to drain blood from the head and aid in healing; and it must be drained with olive oil or myrtle fire, because it is the safest among all veins, because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Therefore, one must seek the easier joint, and not worry if it is necessary to do so for the first time, and one can start again; and sometimes the joints swell in some people when it is necessary for the first time, but it should cause no worry.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the urine is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing that you need to know about bleeding is that it should not be done except to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bleeding should be performed in one of the three veins that are commonly known: namely, the cephalic, femoral, or basilic; and the bleeding should begin during the springtime, at geun, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and the first bleeding should be done on either the first or third day, three hours or four days later.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The first sanitation given for illnesses has no set hour, but when necessary day or night, in every hour and at all times; and it is not appropriate to sanitize children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman bearing a child except during the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One should not treat the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when someone wishes to be sanitized, in any manner that may be, it is required that their intestines be emptied with a light enema, if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not carry waste products to the main organs; nor should one sanitize someone who is overly salty from foods, drunk, or excessively sweating, nor those who are ill from colic, vomiting, stomach problems, excessive urination, heavy labor, staying awake and working, and those who suffer from exhaustion, or from something related to the weapon or body; then soften the humors, if it is too thick, with foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then immerse them in water, unless anything prevents it, to refine the blood, and sanitize the vein on the side opposite the third, as we have said; and keep that day from labor, pain, lust, and similar things; and be careful and cheerful, and let the sanitizer stand higher than the one being sanitized, and rub their arm II or III times, then carefully stretch the sinew above gently, for when it is too tight or narrow, it cannot heal without; then rub the area with the hand until the veins inflate, and feel them; then moisten the sanitizer's fingertip with a little old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand below that vein where he wishes to sanitize, so that the vein does not fail or bleed when cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that resemble ropes in a sieve, and those which are full of windiness, so that when flame is applied, it contracts with the flame, and cannot open the vein; and such cases exist; and if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, therefore the sewer should be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If the vein opens again later or too quickly, and the wound is not inflamed:
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the limb is swollen and the patient fears, let him rest for a day or two and not tie his arm: perhaps pus will come out; do not enter a bath, then resume sewing if it pleases him; and if the puncture is small or narrow, cauterize it carefully and doubt that too much blood will flow from it, and apply the flame directly to the puncture itself; and open it slightly, so that the limb swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the joint swollen, do not start healing immediately, but place a drop of oil on it, as the oil alleviates the body from blood and is thickened in this joint like oil; and administer the oil in every wound where you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same is done with treacle and bandages when applied to the joint; if it becomes too thick, refine it.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if there is a large abscess, which happens often, especially when the opening of the vein is small, hurry up and place a damp sponge soaked in hot vinegar on it and hold for an hour; you must do this after the blood flow from the vein has stopped, and if it remains at the joint after several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not matter; if you see, put something containing aloes or myrrh, refreshed in ashes, powder, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance occur at the base of the basilica; place your hand on it then, if you find it soft to the pressure of the hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be careful not to apply anything mentioned above, for by chance it is in court without the artery; but let it have one dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another medicine until it heals and becomes healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood according to its quantity based on its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red; and if you see it swollen, let it drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for the one who is swollen and protruding, who needs extraction of blood, to make a larger incision; let the veins be wide. And for the weak one, do the opposite, and it should be drained little by little, and it should be drained by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of draining is safe from displacement of blood and compression of nerve, and short drains are more effective than long ones.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 For the one whose body needs draining, give soft bread soaked in pomegranate seeds below; if it is heated, drain the blood 3 or 4 times. And for those of cold complexion, juice the bread before draining with a syrup made from pomegranates or honey-based aromatic syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and make it well-scented.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if it [the wound] festers at the wound site, after much bleeding, then it is necessary that he drink a broth of char, and an aromatic subtle syrup, and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if you want to fracture some bone, and heal it again as needed, when it is weakened by excessive healing, it should heal little by little, according to the quantity of its power continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if you want to fracture some bone after the first healing, and it has strong flesh, it heals seven hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if you want to heal from another part, it should heal on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood inside the body which is already heated and causes fever; in such case it is necessary to draw out a large amount of blood, and to open the sore until it festers at the wound site; then you reward all conditions of healing, and place your hand above the pulse when the wound heals, so that death does not come instead of pus, and this happens many times when healers are negligent; and it is not necessary to dislocate the arm, and to draw blood a second time, and the sore is closed, but you press strongly; nor if it is curved, that you stretch out the arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until the wound heals a second time; or place the tip of the fire at the sore until the congealed blood flows out of the vein, and put a piece of fresh linen on top of it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is burst, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess has been soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the necessity arises to draw blood a second time, do it in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healthier than the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of bleeding is that the patient pushes their hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red; then it should be tied gently, so that the vein appears clearly, then prick it carefully, neither wide nor long; and make large holes, and bleed well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be drained, put the hand back into hot water, and let the blood flow out in the water until you have enough; and if this is a vein, do not pound the hand with hot water again because it puts more winter there than summer; and the bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The vein of the salvation of the right hand is effective for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: Strain the hand, and apply hot water until the vein has fled, if you see it; and if the vein runs sideways, and if you cover it all over, it causes no harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are entirely bare of flesh underneath, then put the hand back in hot water, so that the wound is congealed and cannot leak.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as much as necessary, put oil and linen over the wound to bind it quickly, and do this with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgative of the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do as I have told you regarding the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The vein of the spine is effective for all diseases that are under the body, such as ailments of the back, and retention of phlegm, and diseases of the lungs, and knees and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the qualities of his health are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it over the vein until it perishes, and ties it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot there are many rain-like outflows; therefore, the wider the flow, or at the ankle, is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut open above the foot, guard against the nerves that are beneath, and cut through as well as possible like in cutting; let the flames be still.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the bone cannot come out, place the foot in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 If the vein needs to be treated for the first time, then start again slightly above a finger's breadth as the skin is salty; do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and similarly treat the sole of the other foot in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic nerve is at the knee joint, and its cleaning relieves pain in the ankle, when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the qualities of his health are that the patient immerses himself or herself in water and pulls above the ankle four fingers' breadth while twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, let it be drained in all ways you can, and by crossing; and it is more effective to cut it, for the skin is tough, and it is much obedient to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't treat it, there will be no healing for the pain in the back or side of the foot, and move toward the small toe, and beware of the nerves; and make as much correction of the blood as you see, then undo the bandage, and put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 open abscesses
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Corns or hair, or glass are used for blistering, and blistering is done in two ways: either by making an incision to draw blood, or without making an incision.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 This ventosation that is meant to hurt is of two kinds: one is for all fire, or with fire; the ventosation made by wounding and bloodletting is performed in twelve leagues of the body, from which one is entirely in the head; and the others are under the neck; and the others on both sides of the neck; and the abscesses under the chin; and the abscesses under both shoulders; and the abscesses above the ankles; and the abscesses under both arms; and the abscesses under both legs; and the abscesses under both wrists; and ventosation does not treat blood, unless for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it should not be administered at all, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if due to necessity or custom it is required to bleed, we will do so every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every case; for there are those who, when they need to be bled, have a heavy head; and those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue has swollen, and they bleed; and there are those who dream, and see blood and pains and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially if it is in the month, we order to ventose after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The bleeding of the nose helps with headache ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; and this bleeding is in place of the cephalic bleeding, and those who are of cold complexion should not perform it, or who have a cough, as it does them great harm; and for this reason those with cold head diseases should not perform it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become negligent, and for this reason, the cupping glass should be placed a little lower due to the fear of negligence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is located near the carotid artery and the basilica, and for this reason it is beneficial for pressure, for cutting the channel of the throat, and for complete filling; it must be pressed lightly because if it holds too firmly, it can cause oblique fissure or stomach and heart damage.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosation in the neck towards the chest causes headaches, otalgia and migraines, strangulation, pain at the roots of the teeth, and is located near the carotid artery; you must instruct the patient to press gently with their hand without pressing the artery and not causing bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilations under the chin are useful for mouth diseases and gum decay, as well as other mouth illnesses; they should be placed in the locations of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations under the armpits are useful for diseases that originate from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventosations of the ribs are as much worth as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; instruct the lord not to press too deeply, for the muscles are bare of flesh, and knows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventose on the buttocks is worth as many emorroids from the bottom and diseases below, and it must be large, and made of metal, for it needs to draw well; and in case it is too thin, it will break; and it will cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings in the legs open widely, because they attract blood from all over the body; they are similar to ancient rain sores, scrofula (neck swelling) and bladder stones; they weaken the body after a long time, and bring pus into various conditions. They are located in the area of the knee joints and ankles.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of treating the swelling is to first empty it, suck it quickly, press it evenly, and continue doing so until you see the area turning red and inflamed, and the redness of blood appears; then stop, and place the swellings, and take care in the disposition of the body, because there are some who have thin skin and clear pores: if this is the case, it should be cut once only, and the wounds should be large and deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the skin is thick, it should be cut twice: the first time to make the way for thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very thick, it should be cut three times; and when we want to draw blood drop by drop, we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 If we want much blood, let us often do it; if the flesh is thick, press deeply and limit where the nerves are pierced, and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard, with narrow pores, to anoint the muscles of the ventosations with stimulating and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, use stimulating oil such as violet oil, sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, use oil of parsley, watercress, camomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the person to be healed has a tight and narrow wound, no oil should be put on it, but it should be washed after being lanced with rose water, cold water, lemon water, curds water, or porcelain water, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from bed with the aid of aspen wood, or water of myrtle, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those with excessive fluid stand up from old wine or sour water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or any similar thing; and it should not be sained by lancing before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and they should not sleep after lancing, and it is necessary that they warm themselves, when they must lance and when they have been lanced.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And let him who is recovering from being coleric and excessively sharp and inflamed, take cold things such as green apples, endives and lettuces, and similar items; also, cooked leeks, meat of young cocks, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And one who has a cold constitution should take honey syrup, fragrant wine that is neither old nor new, cooked grapes, and cooked pears and young birds and sparrows; and on the day he farts, he should drink more than eat; also, it is necessary to give some men certain times triacetum or musk to strengthen the main members before or after the farting, and let them be subtle but not too hot for those who drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The ventouses placed to wound are those placed on the liver, spleen, gout, stomach, back, kidneys and loins; for such limbs cannot be wounded elsewhere except to draw blood from one member to another, as we do with the nipples when they are not sore; to remove the viscosity of the member, as we do with a plaster on the stomach or loins to reduce swelling; and to alleviate pain where there is blockage or stone, as it may draw the blockage by accident, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it works when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these ventouses are administered empty for this purpose only; sometimes they are administered with fire, and at other times filled with cold water, like in diseases of the pleura, and in such a way one fills the ventouse with hot liquid or warm liquid in which cooked herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the bladder treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers and a half in width and depth, and have a small hollow around the middle, like pushing an awl, made of bone, soft enough not to prick the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there should be a rod of bone or iron, for placing a splint, and they should be large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who take them; because the blisters of children are different from those of the old, and thin from those who are fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this splint should be placed on the limb in such a way: take the linen or wax splint and place it across the rod within the blister, so that the light is at the bottom of the blister and does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, with the fingers above the hollow that we have mentioned, so that when one looks, one can see the vapor, and remove the blister; and take the linen as before, and repeat it often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder, therefore, which is administered in disease of pleurisy, not having a worm nor an abscess, and it is not brought forth except when it is full of water, and is placed on the member only; this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Sores not brought forth except in members where bladders cannot be administered due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and in bare flesh areas, such as palms or fingertips, and other similar areas; and the nature of the bladder is that when you find sores that are in sweet clear waters without pus, if you take them; put one nut in sweet water with them until they become familiar, and have nothing inside; then let it be drained by bloodletting and bladder, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the sores on it; and when they become full and warm, if it is a place where a bladder can be administered, place it there, for it is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If the shoulder is not in place, lift it up lightly, then press down firmly, and then sprinkle with salt; and if the shoulders remain unhealthy too close to the body, wet a linen cloth with cold water and lay it on, until the sores are dried; and if the sores multiply, lay vitriol powder, or other similar things on them, until they are dried; or you put half-peeled beans on the shoulder and leave them until they adhere to the shoulder, which will now stop the bleeding; and if it requires more care, take other sores.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the sores do not want to take, rub the shoulder with fresh blood, or you insert an awl into them until the sores come out, and then lay them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will clot; and when you see that they are bleeding, pour some powder of aloe and soap or ash over it, which will now stop the bleeding.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
