Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Inform the dear son that foolish men depart from this chapter who have never seen any of the old books, nor read any letters; and because of this, knowledge is alienated in our land, for I have never found it good; and I know nothing about it except through the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated its content, and by experience, and by the habit of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say the summary of this book, the number of words and chapters where the wise put their understanding and dwell on truth, so that those who have been proven knowledgeable will know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 When fracture or dislocation or torsion or curvature comes to anyone, it is necessary that you cleanse the patient from both sides, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of body, or children, or old people; or if the time is not too warm or too cold; and do not eat cold meat, namely cold beef and mutton, nor drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, nor stuff yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you doubt about abscess heat or spread of matter to the member; then the patient returns to their first care as they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that make large stools, or they have thick consistency, such as cooked wheat in water, and peas, and heads, and feet, and pork belly, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment brings on softened stools and the broken bones heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones in the elderly and weak cannot be well regained or sewed according to their nature due to the relaxation of members, neither those who are too tender, such as children's bones; but it does not matter, set on the fractured bone large splints which hold and join the member together, until it heals as it was before; and do not let it touch at all, and therefore nourish it with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breaks are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is different from the break of the foot, or the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of break.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There is a break that grows over time, and another that sharpens, like the quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each type should have its own device and tool in restoration, according to what memory comes to mind; and it is known that the fracture of the bone occurs when the joint is twisted, and it opens widely and swells at the touch; and when there is no twisting or pressure, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have twisting, or fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand, but apply medications that follow, and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fracture which goes into the joint, and are the two parts disjoined, they must now be set equally, so that abscesses may grow in them; and if abscesses grow there, let him leave it for one day, until the abscesses have subsided; then make it equal to the healthy part that you can easily and skillfully adjust, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restorations where there are pieces; then hold it, as needed hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if in the bone there are broken pieces, extend the two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or with your hand a small member, or with two tendons or one tendon and with your hand; and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, adjust all additions in their places as you can, and ensure through your work that no injury or pain comes to the patient; align well the two bones of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you should feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: straighten it out nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring it forth by their work abscess heat and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is set in place, punish the patient well so that he does not move it, neither when watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and be careful that the limb is secure enough so that it feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For if it feels no pain, then it is not set in place, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain; be careful to set it straight so that deformities do not come when it is restored; the qualities of the broken limb are as I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are various in smallness and largeness and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members such as the arm and leg: you should wrap them in soft and thin linen cloth; and those that are thick, like thighs and legs: you should wrap with a wide and stiff rope, for the wide ropes embrace the whole large limb and apply even pressure to all parts so that there is no swelling; then wind strips of bandages lightly around it, 3 or 4 times depending on the member, and hold one part of the rope with your hand, then go above the break and apply less pressure, leaving a gap at the break; and soften the rope a little at a time, taking care to take a large piece of healthy skin; then take another rope and wind it around in the opposite direction over the broken limb; then return to the part below the break, and apply moderate pressure, not too hard or too gently, as we have said in the first lesson above; then place strips of linen or cloth between the ropes, so that they are all even, then bind everything with a bandage and then place well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is a swelling or abscess, place something soothing for the abscess above it and let the swelling be for some days; then press with your poles, and they should be about half the size of a large cane sharpened carefully, or of a stick that is made for splitting wood, or of reeds, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 The poles that one puts on the injury should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and they should be as long as necessary for the limb (whether small or large); then press with your poles in the same way as you did in the first instance, and then bind it with a cord, following the same method as in the first instance on the injury; the binding should be tight at first and less so later; and it should be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, and be made of flax yarn; for if the binding is thick, like I have seen in the works of fools who make their bindings of twisted linen thread, it is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each pole.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is gored by the shafts of arrows after being wounded in healthy limbs, you should place linseed oil or linen cloth on them to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is fractured and the ligaments are torn apart, here is the remedy I shall tell you.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to hold splints on all broken limbs for the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limbs are large, it is not appropriate to put hot irons on them before five or seven days, or more according to your certainty about the abscess healing; and here comes the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: and it is that you take flour that is kept at the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundant egg, and put this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, on, and this is the common method of restoring the fracture for various positions, and similarly for women and small children, because it is neither too cold nor too hot.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for healing fractures, dislocations and twists: take alum, radish, onion, asafetida and arabic gum, mix .x. parts; add myrrh and aloes, .v. parts; 8 parts of alechil; make it into powder, and melt with yolk of egg; if the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of plaster useful for twists: take mugwort and mallow, ten parts; myrrh and aloes, nine parts; cumin Armenian pepper, six parts; mix well, and moisten with vinegar or abundant egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way to splint joints and dislocated bones, relieve the resulting pain, and treat it by cutting the bone, breaking it: take new linen, moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This splint does not restore [the bone], but it is good for relieving abscess heat and bone pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of setting broken bones: take dry fig leaves and ground-up pawpaw (earth-apple) leaves, grind them together to make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to splint for the healing of the fractured bone and for encouraging the return of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take the root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, beeswax flour, from each one a part; grind them together with wine, and if the limbs are scalded, grind it with moist coriander water or vinegar, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of emplastrum (medical plaster) stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of comfrey, flax seeds, balm, clover, wormwood, and chamomile flowers, in equal parts; grind and cook with salt water or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that no other substance should be placed on a broken limb for restoration except for a plaster made of beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between soft and firm but not too soft or too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that dry and slightly warm things should be placed on a broken limb for restoration, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make a plaster for wounds and pain: take mugath and horsehair cut into pieces, or feathers of birds, and almonds, and grind them all together, and make a plaster with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then loosen it a little after some time, and make sure the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved out of its place; do not loosen it for many days. And if pain or pruritus comes to the place, without rest or swelling, hasten, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; take a light cloth and sea sponge wet, dip in water, and rub the place until the pruritus stops, and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it tightly enough to ensure the abscess does not become hot; and let the inflammation of the member subside, and the pain disappear, then continue the binding gently, and a little plaster, and do not strain it too much as before; and apply the binding until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that an abscess has been opened and drained, reddened, painful, and swollen, and you need emplastrum and linen, start it as before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no swelling comes to the limb from what we have said, it should not be dislocated except after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes it is left for twenty days, as I have seen, until the break heals and the joint approaches the flesh; then you must hold it more firmly than before, and thicken its meat, as I said earlier; and if you see the joint drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot enter therein; therefore give it hot, moist heat, every third day, and loosen a little the bandage; by this method you cut off nourishment from the limb, and quickly heal what the foolish surgeon leaves twisted: this is bad, and it is dangerous work, and I see nothing else but to rest and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	In various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of fractures exist and are diverse in their shapes, and the causes are designated; for there are fractures that are made by sword strikes, and the bones at the collar are completely broken up to the shaft which is under the bone, as happens with a cleave or split; and for this reason, such a method of fracture is called "cleavage".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above piercing through, it is called this kind of fracture "absolute"; and these are the two types of fractures, large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impacted percussion, cleavage, fractures from falling on stones, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if the fracture penetrates through to the membrane underneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if the wound is in the bone as fine as hair, and it has a small fissure, it is called this fracture "hairy"; and if the wound is made by being struck by a stone, or falling, or similar things, causing the bone piece to enter below, and the bones are split like a smith when he hammers over pots; if a splinter goes in.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more in those who have a moist skull bone, such as an infant's skull; and it occurs in all kinds of fracture where small bones are displaced, like splinters; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we shall know all ways of breakage by the dislocation above them, and the inquiry into their cause, and by the corruption of the flesh that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy resemblance is known by those who, when the bone has been uncovered and scraped above it, the breakage appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of breakage, beware of the patient's accidents; and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting bile, loss of understanding, extension, paralysis, fever ague, and the eyes to come out and redden, and other similar signs in various dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a doubtful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the navrez comes first to you and it is in winter, then remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the muzzle.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue below the bone is corrupted, and the accidents as we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 If the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, you must cut the broken part as follows: take hold of the patient's head, uncover the bone in all possible ways, and over the wound make an incision more gentle than possible, and if pus or abscess comes out when uncovering the bone, help it with what is needed; and fill the area with damp linen soaked in rose oil; let the wound rest until the pus or abscess subsides and be sure that no more pus comes out; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you make a narrow cut in front, and it is shaped like this:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then insert another cutting tool larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have numerous sizes, some narrow and others wide, sharp and made of iron not pointed; and work lightly, so as not to strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, then you must perforate it around so as to administer sizes with drills, not piercing through the bone of the head, and it should have a margin or one circle above the point that does not let the point pierce through the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each one comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for all bones; and this is the shape of the four types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for perforating around the broken bone are that you place one drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the drill a little further and do this all around, then cut the gap in the bone between the fractures, and do this as delicately as possible, lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or any of the tools you have such as pliers, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you reset the gap that remains between the bone with all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisors; and if something of the small bones or scales remain, do not press hard on them; rather, gently remove them with the instruments; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is that which the Greeks call "saussage," and they hold it in high esteem, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you expose a part of the bone, where the open break moves, so that when you have exposed that part, you place it under the head of this lever-like instrument, as follows in shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut through from one side, but the part should be split into two edges, so that the cut is towards the bone; then hit with a small hammer so that you gently chip around the bone, and take care of the cloth that is beneath it; if it tears against the bone, remove it gently, because it can be chipped badly without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smoothen them out afterwards, and remove the scales with a sharp rasp of various sizes, in order to provide the most suitable solution for each case, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Then pass over with a large rasp, and afterwards with smaller ones, and continue doing so until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each other type of hair-thin fracture and subtle, it is necessary to provide remedy according to its guidance; and this is not something easily understood by one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the wound is open, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled over once or twice, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; do this as lightly as possible so as not to burden the wound, then administer through another linen layer, and do not strain it more than necessary to cover the wound only; leave it like that for a day or two until the abscess subsides, then remove it, and administer medicines such as root of lilies, flour of wheat, incense powder, arsenic, and similar things; from these things make powder and place it on the wound, and administer other reliable medicines without mordication; and be careful that the wound is always clean, do not leave oil or pus in it, nor let it become assembled with a cloth, for when pus gathers on the brain tissue, it corrupts and causes great harm to the patient; for when something mordant is placed on the wound, it breeds more pus.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, if any bad accident happens to the patient as we have said, it is doubtful that he will recover his senses.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness comes violently except for medicine that has been applied to it, whose virtue has been, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and apply the ointment to it; then cure it as necessary until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Sometimes the two parts of the neck above are broken, or one of them only, because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it causes swelling or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 If one of the two parts is broken, you must put your little finger or thumb into the nostril, and place the fracture equal to that part inside the index finger, and at the corner, so that the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part near the neck, and the arm cannot come to its place, then you must align it with the head of a straight stick, about a finger's breadth.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If the fracture is of two parts, you should do the same thing, and hurry to restore it in the first day if possible; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then press the tip of linen cloths at the end of the nose if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you step on one with the other, if it breaks there; and they are so thick that they fill the nostrils of the nose. (Translation)
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said to some restorer that one should moist the tents with butter, and to stir each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem good to me, but they should be moistened in the concoction of egg yolk and flour powder; then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes you step on goose feathers instead of swellings, and if there is a soft cloth around it, and hold the breakage, and blow into the patient's mouth; then do as you please. (Translation)
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess breaks out while you are working on it, put either beeswax or softened cotton in oil of roses, or a pinch of turmeric.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess does not come out, apply plaster from flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then place light drains on it and do not tie them; if the break in the neck is small and broken into small pieces, remove them with appropriate tools, then cut the wound, and treat it with healing ointments or salves suitable for this case; and if there is no wound within the neck, treat it with tents, and place cloth cords on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured beneath and there is no wound outside, and the break is only external, but not broken in two, it is curved within, if this can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary that, if the break is in the right part, you insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the break is in the left jawbone, insert your index finger from the right hand and gently press the break from inside and align it with the other side.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated by 2, then you must administer an extension of 2 parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If the moving of the teeth occurs, whether it's fracture or breakage, hold them with a gold or silver thread or silk, then place a pad on the broken jaw and place one double cloth on top; then place a large well-made bandage or a piece of equal-sized leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it above where you can, and command the patient to rest, and provide him with light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then loosen it on the third day, and then put it back in place what is changed; and apply a poultice over it with flour or mill powder with eggs or linseed meal after removing the pad; and put a light linen on top of the poultice, and if the poultice adheres, and the patient's disposition does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it heals in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess swells up, bring what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, be careful not to remove any bone fragments from the fracture; only remove with cautious instruments suitable for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, dilate it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the bone fragments and there is none left over, stitch up the wound if it is wide, and put on one dressing suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it heals completely.
de la forcele	From the armory (or forceps)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The armory breaks many times in front of the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated into two parts, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatment is when there is a break without an injury, that you have two assistants, one holds the armory where it feels broken; and the other stretches out the neck towards the affected area; then align the break with your hands so that the form is as required, and it has no appearance or bulge.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch more, place a round ball of cloth or linen around the patient's shoulder, as large as necessary; and extend and tighten the armory, and hold the ball with your hand, so that you align the break as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw out the head of the shoulder by force because it comes in fully, then the patient should lie on his affected side and place a small pillow under the shoulder, and the attendant should push the shoulder forward, until the bone of the collarbone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find debris, then you must cut through it; pull the pieces apart gently, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then break it at one of the incisions that you have made; but place this instrument under the collarbone to prevent it from coming out:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it should seem like a ladle, and not narrow, and be as wide as required, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and let it have two prongs, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are sure that the abscess has cooled down, if the opening is small, or if you doubt that the abscess has cooled down, use linen and cotton to dress the wound, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscess becomes cold, immerse it in rose oil and asafoetida and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The setting of the broken bone, when there are wounds and incisions, is that you place a plaster made from mill powder and egg yolk on the bone, put light stoppers over it, and put a splint under the affected area if necessary; then take a very wide bandage, one palm wide, then lay two layers of linen over the stoppers and the plaster; then take a narrow strip of cloth three feet long and wrap it around the bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang out; and place the strip over the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the patient's arm, and under the affected side; and tighten it on each side, and when you see that the bones hold the fracture properly, and you can clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, you should check it every day, and when the linen becomes loose, you should tighten it; place the patient on his back and put a small pillow under the affected area to lift the shoulder up; this will align the fracture of the shoulder blade by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it except for bad accidents, until 20 days have passed; then reapply the plaster if necessary, tighten and leave it like that until it is healed; and it is usually healed in 28 days, but in fewer days for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It is necessary that the shoulder break or dislocate not heal on its own, and one can only force it back with touching; then arrange it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it in accordance with its natural form, in all possible ways; then place powder from a mill on the joint with plenty of egg, light bandages, and put it under a double cloth; then put a large and delicate splint over it, about one finger wider than the shoulder, and if there are any hollows anywhere on the shoulder beneath the splint, fill them with linen bandages so that the splint fits evenly; and then bind it tightly with a great bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and watch the ligament every day; and whenever it softens, bind it again, and make the splint equal if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be reset in twenty or twenty-five days, and when this number is completed, loosen it, and be sure, for it is not bone that easily becomes dislocated.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front, but not underneath the skin, lift it up and remove the bone, and follow what was said earlier in the setting of a fracture to treat an abscess with hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture (of the) thigh
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The injury is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the back.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 When it is broken in the middle, it declines below and causes the patient great pain, and lack of nourishment, and immediately vomits blood, and opens the fractures in the bones that are broken, and he feels it all very acutely.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and one places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides to your hands, and subtly puts it all in place in all ways possible until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then put splints and pillows over the thin part of the bone where salt or another light substance is, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; then turn the ligament round and round towards the back, and tighten it gradually, and check every hour if it has healed, and if it softens, tighten it again; and if it needs to be untied, due to corrosion or itchiness at the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, remove the splint, and attend to those who have come in matters of cures; then reset the splint, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs occurs only in large ones behind the back and near the chest, and they do not bend unless because they are slippery; and it is felt well at the inquiry of the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the restoration is that you set the fracture equally as necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then put a splint, and tighten it with a stick if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the fracture of the ribs is inclined inward, causing great pain and swelling, similar to pleurisy, for the bone pierces the lung; and it swells at the tips, and immediately vomits a large amount of blood, which is a sign of grave illness, and the ancients had used much effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the abdomen in order to push out the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot irons come if they have not arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, make them healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say to put leeches on the joint for swelling, which seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the leech does not attract the excess to the joint due to its weak constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say to cover the joint with damp linen in hot oil and put tents between the ribs to make it equal on all sides; then it should be cured with pleurisy cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the patient feels intense pain that he cannot bear on the bone that is not covered by fabric, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to make an incision above the level of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put something under the instrument to prevent infection; and then you must split the bone, extract it lightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat the wound with splints until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when an abscess swells up, lay on it a moistened cloth soaked in rose oil, and place the heat source over it; cure the abscess as required, and let the patient lie still on the side where it is located until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes breaks occur in the collarbone bones and they bend; and likewise in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And if this happens and you want to know whether it will be healed or not, take note if his hands become softened, swollen, and dead, and he cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, there is no pain felt.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in many ways, and if the hands are silent and feel well when they are pulled or pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and that the patient should be cured if care is taken.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing happens at the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is hollow or not, beware if the feet are soft, and if there is an accident that is in hands, and over the back sudden swelling and evacuation without will; and when it has been prodded on the stomach, there is evacuation without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And if it is prodded on the back and it wants to heal, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is mortal: do not labor at its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen to him, it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply oil to a hot abscess, either rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it is soothed; then apply one of the comforting and drying ointments, bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, you must cover it with oil; then remove the bone, join the two sides of the wound together with stitches, if it is large, until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow", put your left hand in its place and hold it equal to your right hand, then apply the ointment and plaster if necessary; then tie it, and if it dislocates again, push it back into place, remove the bone, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the leg bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the bone of the shin is broken, and if it happens, there is only a little lessening at the head; and it becomes long, declines to the front, comes to the patient pain at the place, and points and swells where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the break; and recognize which one is the break and its shape; and if the break is at the head only, then make an equal incision in the same natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or declines within, then make the patient lie on his belly, so that the restoration of the break is presented to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight (the dislocation), put a splint above it, then put a stick or a rod on top and hold the break so that it does not move; and apply the area below the ribs until the breaks are level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess swells up, do not touch it until the abscess swelling subsides, and put on what was previously mentioned (the bandage); then return to treatment, and hold it as needed, without any bad incident occurring; and that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is between the chest and the neck of the upper arm, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways: of which one is that you take a splint thicker than a thumb, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads together with two ropes, and bind them upwards, and make the patient lie on one seat; then let him throw his broken arm over the splint, until it comes to rest, and have a hump of splint in the middle, then bind above something heavy or the minister extends it downward; then put the mirrors the break even with their hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that one restrains the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two servants that one holds the one who is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below along all the limb, and extends each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 If you see that the extraction is too strong, hold the ligament under the break, and above the break, and extend each of the attendants to their own part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the neck of the shoulder, then you must place the splint underneath the neck and the other side towards the break; and similarly, if the break is towards the side, then you must gently place the splint, without effort, so that the break is level with its place and with the side; then make the break equal, as needed, and hold it in place, unless an abscess develops.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If abscesses have come up, do not hold it for more than 7 days, and place soft linen cloth soaked in rose oil on it until the abscesses are calm; then hold it, and the method of holding it is that you put a wooden splint on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and tie the bandage, and hold it on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in its normal position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use a probe, and place a larger and stronger probe over the fracture, with one inch of space between each probe, and let each probe be as wide as it passes the fracture two inches from each side; then hold the probes in place, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, firmly and slightly less in alignment.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the position of the bones and the compression, as we have said, during the time that you are restoring the broken limb, and you doubt an abscess forming, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine every three days the binding, to ensure pus does not swell or come to the place, nor the blood flow to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accidents occur, the dislocation should not be treated before three days or more have passed, and the patient should lie on his back with his hands on his stomach; and place a linen bandage of equal thickness beneath the shoulder, and observe every hour of the day or night that the limb does not move or become softened ligaments; treat it with the direction through the power of medicine, and give him the meat as previously specified, in such a way that the meat is at first tender; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be set in 40 days altogether; and then you must dislocate it again and administer a bath and ointments to guide its direction.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the stricture is deformed and blocked, it will take days or two months to dissolve.
de la brisure du bras	In case of a broken arm:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "forearm," of which one is small and forms the lower part of the elbow; and the other is large, and is located under it near the little finger. By chance, only the large forearm may break or both, and sometimes they break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small boils are broken, the restoration and healing are easy; but when the large ones are broken, the healing is poor, and more difficult than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small boil that has been broken, one should extend it slightly and make it level.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large boil, one should tighten it more forcefully; extend it over the spoon, and place the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the patient lie crosswise on top of it, and the spoon in front of it be raised higher so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch out the attendants' arms to the part below his hand or his leg, and one attendant at the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the mirror adjusts it to its equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If the break is in several places, put each one back in its place, and if there is any displacement that pricks the bone, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if it is wounded by breaking, I have spoken about it in the individual chapter; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 If at the beginning of the resetting there are abscesses boiled, apply a thin cloth made of rosin oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; adhere the cloth to it gently until the abscess is soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 Then remove the rosin cloth, and apply a plaster made of milled powder with plenty of egg, then insert the splints; the splint of the fracture should be more prominent than the others, and slightly larger; it must have six splints or more in different positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two.
