And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and try to feel in the part where it is dislocated: repositioning should be gentle, and it must be gently stretched with hands when only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit straight, and hold him by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, then to the left hand twice, then lift it up, and push the foot up forcefully; do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, restart the process, as it may return; and if it cannot return, place the patient on his back on the ground, and fix the splint firmly in the ground between his knees, and cover it with rags so as not to hurt the patient; then hold the knee, and another person holds the foot at the ankle or the shin, keeping it raised above the foot; each person holds equally, and the splint should be close between the patient's knees to keep the patient when lifting him; then place mirrors equal to the dislocation in their hands, and another person holds the leg straight below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is at the point, put the plaster and poultice on top, press firmly, and tie the leg to the foot, and watch the nerves that are above the heel behind, that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage softens, straighten it; then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and let the patient walk for four days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess opens, you must calm it, as we have said elsewhere, until it heals.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, they must be stretched out gently without effort, and it is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any way towards the back of the foot, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or a bed straight up, and put your foot above the joints, then press firmly until it returns; and when it is even and there is no gap, place a two-fingered table under the foot sole, then tighten it, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and it is to be restored, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, unless you are wise in the art and have long used it; and be compassionate, merciful, and slow; do not be hasty; and first use warm poultices on the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of healing; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the poultice arrives where it should; and when the limb is in place, administer warm poultices to the abscess, heal the wound as necessary, using strongly desiccated herbs; and if with dislocation there is a break, and small bones are displaced, set them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware of entering into fear, as I have said, for it will harm you according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your weapons and body.
Amen	 Amen (So be it)
